وَحَطَّ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ سَمَاءِ العَقْلِ كُلَّ حِجَابٍ مِنْ سَحَابِ الجَهْلِ. المَعْنَوِيَّةِ مَجَازاً بِالِاسْتِعَارَةِ؛ لِعَلَاقَةِ: المُشَابَهَةِ، وَاشْتُقَ مِنْهُ : حَطَ بِمَعْنَى : أَزَاحَ إِزَاحَةٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الاسْتِعَارَةِ التَّبِعِيَّةِ. قَوْلُهُ : (عَنْهُمْ) أَيْ: عَنْ أَرْبَابِ الحِجَا . وَقَوْلُهُ : (مِنْ) سَمَاءِ العَقْلِ بَدَلٌ مِنَ الجَارِّ وَالمَجْرُورِ قَبْلَهُ ؛ بَدَلُ اشْتِمَالٍ، أَوْ بَدَلُ بَعْضٍ مِنْ كُلِّ، وَالأَوَّلُ أَقْرَبُ . وَ(مِنْ)) وَ مِنْ بِمَعْنَى : «عَنْ» عَلَى مَذْهَبِ الكُوفِيِّينَ ؛ مِنْ تَجْوِيزِ نِيَابَةِ بَعْضِ الحُرُوفِ عَنْ بَعْضٍ. وَأَشَارَ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ إِلَى أَنَّ إِضَافَةَ سَمَاءِ إِلَى العَقْلِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ إِلَى المُشَبِّهِ. وَالأَصْلُ: «مِنَ العَقْلِ الَّذِي هُوَ كَالسَّمَاءِ؛ بِجَامِعِ : أَنَّ كُلًّا مَحَلٌّ لِطُلُوعِ الشَّمُوسِ. قوله : (مَجَازاً بِالِاسْتِعَارَةِ هذا لا يتعيَّن بل يصح أن يكون مرسلاً لعلاقة التقييد ثم الإطلاق؛ بأن تطلق الإزاحة الحسيَّة عن التّقييد بالحسيَّة، وتستعمل فى المعنوية. ولك أن تقول : ليس هنا إلا مجاز واحدٌ؛ بأن يُنقل الحظ عن الإزاحة الحسيَّة مِن عُلْوِ إِلَى سُفْلِ إلى مطلق إزاحة حسيَّة أو لا، من علو إلى سفل أو لا، ويستعمل في المعنوية؛ لكونها فرداً من الأفراد. قوله : بَدَلٌ مِنَ الجَارِّ وَالمَجْرُورِ قَبْلَهُ. . إلخ) ويحتمل أيضاً أن تكون «من» للتعليل والسَّببيَّة ؛ أي: أزال عنهم بسبب عقلهم . قوله : (وَالأَوَّلُ أَقْرَبُ) أي : مِن جعله بدل بعض ؛ لأنَّ العقل صفة لا جزء. اهـ شيخنا المؤلّف. فإن قلت : إنَّ بدل الاشتمال لا بدَّ له من رابط، ولا رابط هنا . قلت : أجيب عن ذلك بجوابين : الأوَّل : أنَّ «أَلْ» بدل عن المضاف إليه ؛ أي: عن عقلهم كما هو مذهب الكوفيين. الثَّاني : أنَّ الرَّابط مقدَّرُ ، والتَّقديرُ : مِن سماء العقل لهم، كما هو مذهب البصريين. وَإِنْ كَانَ العَقْلُ مَحَلَّا لِطُلُوعِ الشُّمُوسِ المَعْنَوِيَّةِ - الَّتِي هِيَ أُصُولُ المَعَارِفِ وَأُمَّهَاتُهَا ـ ، وَالسَّمَاءُ مَحَلَّا لِطُلُوعِ الشُّمُوسِ الحِسيَّة. وَجَوَّزَ بَعْضُهُمْ: أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي كَلَامِهِ اسْتِعَارَةٌ بِالكِنَايَةِ ؛ قَالَ : بِأَنْ يُشَبَّهَ العَقْلُ بِالفَلَكِ الأَعْظَمِ ؛ تشبيهاً مُضْمَراً فِي النَّفْسِ ، وَيُحْذَفُ، وَيُثْبَتُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ لَوَازِمِهِ وَهُوَ السَّمَاءُ تَخْيِيلاً . وَنُوقِشَ : بِأَنَّ السَّمَاءَ لَيْسَتْ مِنْ لَوَازِمِ الفَلَكِ الأَعْظَمِ وَخَوَاصٌهِ، بَلْ هِيَ جِرْمَ آخَرُ مُسْتَقِل. قوله : (وَإِنْ كَانَ العَقْلُ مَحَلَّا لِطُلُوعِ الشُّمُوسِ المَعْنَوِيَّةِ فيه: أنَّ المحل إنَّما هو النَّفس؛ لأنها هي المدركة، وأمَّا العقل فهو آلةٌ كما تقدَّم. إلَّا أن يقال : المراد بـ «العقل هنا : النَّفس، أو أنَّ الآلة قد تتّصف بكونها محلًّا لِمَا هي آلة فيه . قوله : (وَجَوَّزَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي كَلَامِهِ اسْتِعَارَةُ بِالكِنَايَةِ ... إلخ) ويجوز أيضاً أن يكون في كلامه استعارة تصريحيَّة؛ بأن يشبه القلب بالسَّماء؛ بجامع: أنَّ كلَّا محلّ لِمَا يُنتفع به، فإنَّ القلب محل للعقل، والسَّماءَ محل للكواكب التي يُهتدى بها . هذا بناءً على أنَّ العقل في القلب، فإن بنينا على أنَّه في الرّأس، فتشبه الرأس بالسَّماء؛ بجامع: أنَّ كلا محل لما ينتفع به، وعلى كل يُستعار اسم المشبه به للمشبَّه على طريق التّصريحية، والقرينة: الإضافة إلى العقل . قوله : (بِالفَلَكِ الأَعْظَم) وهو العرش. قوله : (وَنُوقِشَ : بِأَنَّ السَّمَاءَ» لَيْسَتْ مِنْ لَوَازِمِ الفَلَكِ ... إلخ) قيل : إنَّها من لوازمه بحسب الوجود ؛ لأنَّ العرش فوق السَّماء وجوداً .
And He removed from them, from the sky of the intellect, every veil of the clouds of ignorance. [The removal] is metaphorical by metaphor, due to the relation of resemblance, and derived from it is 'hatta' meaning 'he removed' an abstract removal by way of derivative metaphor. His statement: 'from them' means: from the people of intelligence. And his statement: 'from the sky of the intellect' is a substitute for the preceding prepositional phrase; a substitution of inclusion, or a substitution of part from whole, and the first is closer. And 'min' [here] means 'from' according to the Kufan school, allowing one particle to substitute for another. The author indicated in his commentary that the idafa of 'sky' to 'intellect' is of the type of idafa of the thing compared to to the thing compared. The original is: 'from the intellect which is like the sky', with the common factor being that each is a place for the rising of suns. Al-Anbabi: His statement: 'metaphorically by metaphor' is not determined; rather it is permissible that it be a synecdoche due to the relation of restriction then generalization: by releasing the physical removal from its restriction to the physical and using it in the abstract. Or you could say there is only one figure here: by transferring the 'hatt' from physical removal from above to below to absolute physical removal (or not, from above to below or not) and using it in the abstract because it is an individual instance. His statement: 'a substitute for the preceding prepositional phrase etc.' It is also possible that 'min' is for cause and reason, i.e., he removed from them because of their intellect. His statement: 'the first is closer' means than making it a substitution of part, because the intellect is an attribute not a part. So said our teacher the author. If you say: substitution of inclusion requires a linker, and there is no linker here. I say: it is answered with two answers: first, that 'al' is a substitute for the genitive attached, i.e., 'their intellect' as per the Kufan school. Second, that the linker is implicit, the estimation being: 'from the sky of the intellect for them', as per the Basran school. And although the intellect is a place for the rising of spiritual suns - which are the principles and mothers of knowledge - and the sky is a place for the rising of physical suns. Some allowed that in his speech there is an implicit metaphor: by comparing the intellect to the greatest sphere, an implicit comparison in the mind, omitting it and establishing something from its concomitants, which is 'sky', as a fictional extension. And it was objected: that the sky is not among the concomitants and properties of the greatest sphere; rather it is an independent body. Al-Anbabi: His statement: 'And although the intellect is a place for the rising of spiritual suns' contains: that the locus is actually the soul, because it is the perceiver, whereas the intellect is an instrument as previously stated. Unless it is said what is meant by 'intellect' here is the soul, or that the instrument can be described as a locus for that of which it is an instrument. His statement: 'Some allowed that in his speech there is an implicit metaphor...' It is also permissible that in his speech there is an explicit metaphor: by comparing the heart to the sky, with the common factor that each is a place for beneficial things: the heart is a place for the intellect, and the sky is a place for the stars by which guidance is obtained. This is based on the intellect being in the heart. If we base it on it being in the head, then the head is compared to the sky. In either case, the name of the thing compared to is borrowed for the thing compared in the explicit way, and the clue is the idafa to 'intellect'. His statement: 'the greatest sphere' meaning the Throne. His statement: 'It was objected: that the sky is not among the concomitants of the sphere...' It was said: but it is among its concomitants in terms of existence, because the Throne is above the sky in existence.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq: 'And He removed from them, from the sky of the intellect, every veil of the clouds of ignorance.' The commentators provide grammatical and rhetorical analysis. Al-Bajuri explains that 'hatta' (removed) is used metaphorically (isti'ara) for abstract removal, derived from physical removal. The phrase 'from them' refers to people of intelligence (arbab al-hija). He then discusses the grammatical status of 'min sama' al-'aql' (from the sky of the intellect), suggesting it is a substitution (badal) for the previous prepositional phrase, either badal ishtimal (substitution of inclusion) or badal ba'd min kull (substitution of part from whole), preferring the former because the intellect is an attribute, not a part. He also notes that 'min' might mean 'from' (an) according to Kufan grammar, allowing prepositions to stand for one another. The idafa (construct phrase) 'sama' al-'aql' is explained as a metaphor: the intellect is like the sky in that each is a locus for the rising of 'suns' (physical and spiritual). Al-Anbabi then adds nuance: the metaphor might not be a pure isti'ara but a mursal (synecdoche) based on restriction and generalization. He also proposes another interpretation: the entire expression is a single metaphor, transferring 'hatt' from physical removal to any removal. He discusses whether 'min' indicates causation, i.e., 'because of their intellect'. On page 70, the discussion continues with the metaphor of the intellect as a place for spiritual suns (principles of knowledge). Some scholars suggest a different metaphor: isti'ara bil-kinaya (implicit metaphor), comparing the intellect to the 'greatest sphere' (the Throne), with 'sky' as a concomitant detail. This is criticized: the sky is not a necessary part of the sphere. Al-Anbabi then offers alternatives: an explicit metaphor (tashrihiyya) comparing the heart or head to the sky, depending on whether the intellect resides in the heart or head. The passage thus meticulously unpacks the rhetorical and grammatical layers of the opening line.

Key Terms
حط (hatta): Used metaphorically to mean abstract removal of ignorance, derived from physical downward movement. [Note: No significant shift; stable in Arabic lexica.]
استعارة (isti'ara): Metaphor, transferring a word from its literal meaning to figurative based on resemblance. [Note: Standard term in Arabic rhetoric; no shift in the logic tradition.]
بدل (badal): Grammatical substitution, where a phrase replaces another to clarify or specify. [Note: Standard in Arabic grammar; stable.]
سماء العقل (sama' al-'aql): Metaphorical phrase for the elevated realm of intellect, likened to the sky as a locus for rising 'suns' (knowledge). [Note: Specific to this commentary; not a standard logical term.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the commentary, what is the grammatical function of 'من سماء العقل' in the opening line of al-Sullam?
A) It is a direct object.
B) It is a substitution (badal) for the preceding prepositional phrase.
C) It is an adverb of place.

Key Takeaway
The opening line of al-Sullam is a carefully crafted metaphor that condenses the entire purpose of logic, and understanding its linguistic layers is essential for proper comprehension.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Analyzing Idāfah and Metaphor in Sullam's Opening Line
Commentators analyze rhetorical devices and idāfah in Sullam's opening line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the type of idāfah and metaphor in a given Arabic phrase from the logical tradition and determine the referent of pronouns accordingly.

Core Idea
The same line can yield different metaphorical interpretations depending on idāfah analysis.

Al-Bajūrī's commentary on the opening line of Sullam al-Munawraq reveals how a single poetic phrase can be read through multiple metaphorical lenses. Understanding the interplay between idāfah (construct phrase) and isti'ārah (metaphor) is key to grasping the deeper meanings intended by the author. This lesson will walk you through the two main interpretations presented and show how each affects pronoun reference and overall meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the idāfah structure
The phrase 'shumūs al-ma'rifah' is a construct (idāfah). Determine whether the first term (mudāf) is the likened-to (mushabbah bih) and the second (mudāf ilayh) is the likened (mushabbah), or whether the idāfah is partitive (min al-tab'īḍiyyah).
The commentator presents both possibilities.
2
Determine the type of metaphor
If the suns are left literal, the metaphor is implicit (makniyyah). If the suns are themselves a metaphor for the issues (masā'il), the metaphor becomes explicit (musarrahah) or remains implicit but with a different reference.
The qarīnah (contextual indicator) is the idāfah to the pronoun.
3
Check pronoun reference
In the first interpretation, the pronoun in 'mukhaddarātihā' must refer to 'al-ma'rifah' (knowledge), not the suns. The rule that pronouns refer to the nearest antecedent is only predominant, not absolute, as shown by Qur'anic evidence.
This is a key insight from al-Bajūrī.
4
Interpret the derived metaphor for mukhaddarāt
The term 'mukhaddarāt' is a derived explicit metaphor (isti'ārah taṣrīḥiyyah taba'iyyah) based on likening concealment to a woman behind a curtain. Identify the commonality (jāmi') of non-appearance.
This shows how metaphors are created from root words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلَى جَعْلِ الإِضَافَةِ فِي شُمُوسِ المَعْرِفَةِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّهِ. وَكَذَا عَلَى جَعْلِ كَلَامِهِ مِنْ بَابِ الِاسْتِعَارَةِ المَكْنِيَّةِ إِذَا جُعِلَتِ الشُّمُوسُ بَاقِيَةٌ عَلَى مَعْنَاهَا الحَقِيقِي؛ إِذِ الصَّمِيرُ حِينَئِذٍ يَتَعَيَّنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ رَاجِعاً لِلمَعْرِفَةِ، وَلَا تَرِدُ القَاعِدَةُ المَذْكُورَةُ؛ لِأَنَّهَا أَغْلَبِيَّةٌ؛ بِدَلِيلِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَادْخُلُوا أَبْوَابَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا﴾ [الزمر: ٧٢]. بِخِلَافِ : جَعَلِ الكَلَام مِنْ بَابِ الاِسْتِعَارَةِ المُصَرَّحَةِ، وَكَذَا المَكْنِيَّةِ إِنْ جُعِلَتِ الشُّمُوسُ مُسْتَعَارَةٌ لِلمَسَائِلِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَصِحُ حِينَئِذٍ رُجُوعُ الضَّمِيرِ لِلشُّمُوسِ، وَتَكُونُ الإِضَافَةُ عَلَى مَعْنَى: (مِنْ) التَّبعِيضِيَّة، وَالمَعْنَى: رَأوا المَسَائِلَ الخَفِيَّةَ مِنْهَا. ثُمَّ إِنَّ المُخَدَّرَاتِ جَمْعُ: مُخَدَّرَةٍ، وَهِيَ: المَرْأَةُ المُسْتَتِرَةُ تَحْتَ الخِدْرِ، لَكِنَّ المُرَادَ: مِنَ المُخَدَّرَاتِ هُنَا: المَسَائِلُ الخَفِيَّةُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الاِسْتِعَارَةِ التَّصْرِيحِيَّةِ التَّبَعِيَّةِ، وَذَلِكَ بِأَنْ يُشَبَّهَ الخَفَاءُ بِمَعْنَى التَّخْدِيرِ؛ بِجَامِعِ: عَدَمِ الظُّهُورِ فِي كُلِّ، وَيُسْتَعَارُ لَفْظُ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّهِ، ثُمَّ يُشْتَقُ مِنْهُ مُخَدَّرَاتٍ بِمَعْنَى: خَفِيَّاتٍ، وَالقَرِينَةُ: الإِضَافَةُ إِلَى الضَّمِيرِ العَائِدِ إِلَى المَعْرِفَةِ أَوِ الشُمُوسِ عَلَى مَا عَلِمْتَ، وَالرُّؤْيَةُ: تَرْشِيحٌ، وَكَذَا الإِنْكِشَافُ إِنْ كَانَ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الحِرِّيَّاتِ فَقَطْ.
Concerning making the idāfah in 'shumūs al-ma'rifah' as the idāfah of the likened-to for the likened. Likewise concerning making his statement [the line] from the category of implicit metaphor when the suns are left upon their real meaning; for then the pronoun is necessarily determined to refer to knowledge, and the mentioned rule does not apply because it is only predominant, as evidenced by His saying: 'And enter the gates of Hell to abide therein forever' (az-Zumar 72). Contrary to making the statement from the category of explicit metaphor, and likewise implicit metaphor if the suns are made a metaphor for the issues, for then it is valid for the pronoun to refer to the suns, and the idāfah is upon the meaning of partitive 'min', and the meaning is: they saw the hidden issues among them. Then indeed 'al-mukhaddarāt' is the plural of 'mukhaddarah', which is a woman concealed behind a curtain, but the intended meaning of 'al-mukhaddarāt' here is the hidden issues by way of derived explicit metaphor. That is by likening concealment to the meaning of hiding behind a curtain, due to the commonality of non-appearance in each, and the word of the likened-to is borrowed for the likened, then derived from it 'mukhaddarāt' meaning 'hidden ones'. The qarīnah is the idāfah to the pronoun referring to knowledge or the suns as you have learned. 'ar-ru'yah' is tarshīh, and likewise 'al-inkishāf' if it is literal only for physical unveilings.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the commentary on the opening line of the Sullam al-Munawraq. The commentator, al-Bajūrī, discusses two interpretations of the idāfah in 'shumūs al-ma'rifah' and the nature of the metaphor in the line. First, if the idāfah is considered as adding the likened-to (the suns) to the likened (knowledge), then the suns remain literal, and the metaphor is implicit (makniyyah). In this case, the pronoun in 'mukhaddarātihā' must refer to 'al-ma'rifah' (knowledge), not the suns. The rule that pronouns typically refer to the nearest antecedent is only predominant, not absolute, as shown by Qur'anic usage. Second, if the suns are themselves a metaphor for the issues (masā'il), then the metaphor becomes explicit (musarrahah) or implicit with a different pronoun reference, and the idāfah is partitive ('min'), meaning they saw some hidden issues. The passage then defines 'mukhaddarāt' as a derived term from 'mukhaddarah' (hidden woman), metaphorically applied to hidden issues. The metaphorical process is explained: concealment is likened to hiding behind a curtain due to shared absence of appearance, the word for the physical veil is borrowed, and the derived form 'mukhaddarāt' is coined meaning 'hidden ones'. The qarīnah (indicator) is the idāfah to the pronoun. The words 'ru'yah' (seeing) and 'inkishāf' (unveiling) are tarshīh (reinforcing imagery) if taken literally.

استعارة مكنية
مخدرات

Checkpoint
In the interpretation where the suns are left literal (isti'ārah makniyyah), to which noun does the pronoun in 'mukhaddarātihā' necessarily refer?
A) The suns (al-shumūs)
B) Knowledge (al-ma'rifah)
C) The issues (al-masā'il)
D) The hidden ones (al-mukhaddarāt)

Key Takeaway
The same Arabic construct can sustain multiple metaphorical interpretations; the choice of idāfah type and pronominal reference is governed by contextual indicators and not by mechanical rules.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Purpose of Double Praise in Islamic Texts
Bajuri and Anbabi explain why the author praised twice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the structural and prophetic reasons for using both nominal and verbal praise in the opening of a text, and identify the rhetorical device of tarshih.

Core Idea
Double praise is not redundancy; it combines two sentence types for reward and follows the Prophet's example.

In the opening of many Islamic works, authors often praise Allah twice: once implicitly through a nominal sentence and once explicitly through a verbal sentence. This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary explains the reason behind this practice. Let's explore the rhetorical and legal wisdom behind this double praise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of praise
Notice that the author praised Allah twice: once with a nominal sentence (implicit in 'al-hamdu lillah') and once with a verbal sentence ('nahmaduhu'). The nominal sentence indicates permanence, the verbal indicates renewal.
2
Find the prophetic precedent
Al-Bajuri tells us that this double praise follows the hadith: 'Indeed praise is due to Allah, we praise Him.' The Prophet combined both forms, so the author is following the sunna.
3
Understand the purpose of combining both
The author combined them 'to drink from each of the two cups' – i.e., to obtain the reward of both nominal and verbal praise. This is not redundancy but a deliberate act of devotion.
4
Recognize the rhetorical device tarshih
The commentary mentions 'tarshih' – reinforcement of a metaphor. The double praise also serves to reinforce the meaning and create a balanced rhetorical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (نَحْمَدُهُ ... إلخ) إِنَّمَا حَمِدَهُ مَرَّتَيْنِ (۳) : إِحْدَاهُمَا بِالجُمْلَةِ الاِسْمِيَّةِ، وَالأُخْرَى بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ:
- تأسياً بِحَدِيثِ: «إِنَّ الحَمْدَ اللَّهِ نَحْمَدُهُ (۳)
- وَجَمْعاً بَيْنَ الأَمْرَيْنِ - أَعْنِي : الحَمْدَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الاِسْمِيَّةِ ، وَالحَمْدَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ - ؛ لِيَشْرَبَ بِكُلِّ مِنَ الكَاسَيْنِ ؛ أَيْ : لِيُحَصِّلَ ثَوَابَ الحَمْدِ
قوله : (لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَلُ هُنَا إِلَّا فِي مَفْعُولٍ وَاحِدٍ) أي: لأنَّها بصريَّةٌ وتسليط الرُّؤية البصرية على المخدرات التي بمعنى المسائل مبالغة، كما هو شأن الترشيح، أو الكلام على تقدير مضافين؛ أي: رأوا دَال دالّها، وهو النقوش الدَّالَّة على الألفاظ، الدَّالَّة على المعاني.
وإِنَّما لم يجعل رأى قلبيَّةٌ؛ لأنَّه ليس المعنى على ذلك؛ لأنَّه يصير المعنى : علموا انكشافها، وهذا ليس بمقصود) ، إنَّما المقصود إبصارها لهم في حال انكشافها . وقد يقال : يلزمُ من علمهم انكشافها لهم علمها حالة كونها منكشفة؛ إلا أن يقال: المقصود بالذكر هو الأولى؛ خصوصاً في مقام البيان للمبتدئ؛ تدبَّر .
His statement: (We praise Him... etc.) Indeed he praised Him twice: one with a nominal sentence and the other with a verbal sentence — following the hadith: 'Indeed praise is due to Allah, we praise Him' — and combining the two matters, I mean praise with a nominal sentence and praise with a verbal sentence, so that he may drink from each of the two cups, i.e. to obtain the reward of praise. His statement: (because it [ru'ya] does not act here except on one object) i.e. because it is visual, and directing the visual sight to the 'mukhadarat' which mean issues is an exaggeration, as is the nature of reinforcement (tarshih), or the speech is on the assumption of two omitted words: i.e. they saw the indicator of its indicators, which are the marks that indicate the words that indicate the meanings. And 'ra'a' was not made heart-sight because the meaning is not that; because it would become 'they knew its unveiling', and this is not intended. The intended is only their seeing it in the state of its unveiling. It may be said: it follows from their knowing its unveiling that they know it in the state of being unveiled, except that it is said: the intended in mentioning is the former, especially in the context of explanation for the beginner; reflect.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage explains the second line of the matn: 'Nahmaduhu jalla 'ala al-in'am...' al-Bajuri begins by stating that the author praised Allah twice: once with a nominal sentence (implicitly) and once with a verbal sentence (the explicit 'nahmaduhu'). The reason for this is twofold: first, following the hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet praised with both (al-hamdu lillahi nahmaduhu); second, to combine both forms and thereby obtain the reward of praise from both. Then al-Anbabi adds a commentary on the earlier line about 'ra'aw' (they saw). He argues that 'ra'a' is visual, not heart-sight (qalbiyya), because making it heart-sight would yield 'they knew its unveiling', which is not the intended meaning; the intended is actual sight in the state of unveiling. He also notes that if it were heart-sight, there would be no exaggeration, and the meaning would be redundant with 'until the suns of knowledge appeared'. The commentary includes a marginal note from al-Shirshimi reinforcing that 'ra'a' is visual, and that the intended meaning is actual sight, not knowledge.

Key Terms
الجملة الاسمية
الجملة الفعلية
ترشيح

A) To make the poem longer
B) To follow the hadith and combine nominal and verbal praise
C) To correct a mistake
D) To emphasize the meaning of 'al-hamdu lillah' only

Key Takeaway
The double praise combines nominal and verbal forms to follow the hadith and to obtain reward from both types of sentences.

Introduction and Front Matter

Why the Double Praise? Nominal and Verbal Sentences
Bajuri explains the double praise in the opening of al-Sullam al-Munawraq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author uses both nominal and verbal sentences in the opening praise, based on the principle of rhetorical suitability (munasaba) between sentence type and the object of praise.

Core Idea
Sentence type mirrors the nature of what is praised: permanent essence vs. renewed blessings.

The opening praise in al-Sullam al-Munawraq is not redundant—each sentence is carefully chosen. Bajuri unpacks the wisdom behind using a nominal sentence for the first praise and a verbal sentence for the second. By understanding this, you gain insight into how Arabic grammar and rhetoric serve theological expression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two praise sentences
Locate the two forms: the implied nominal sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' (praise be to Allah) and the explicit verbal sentence 'nahmaduhu' (we praise Him). Notice that the first is a statement (noun-initial), the second an action (verb-initial).
The author follows the hadith: 'Inna al-hamda lillah nahmaduhu'.
2
Determine the object of each praise
The commentator states that the first praise is for Allah's Essence (al-dhat)—eternal and unchanging. The second praise is for His bestowal of blessings (al-in'am)—renewed moment by moment.
This distinction is key to understanding the choice.
3
Connect sentence type to meaning
In Arabic, nominal sentences indicate permanence and stability; verbal sentences indicate renewal and gradual occurrence. Match this: Essence is permanent → nominal sentence. Bestowal is renewed → verbal sentence.
This is a principle of balagha (rhetoric), not just grammar.
4
Assess why both are needed
The combination allows the reader to gain the reward of both forms and to praise Allah comprehensively—for Who He is and for what He does. Each sentence type is uniquely suited to its object.
The commentator likens it to drinking from two cups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (نَحْمَدُهُ ... إلخ) إِنَّمَا حَمِدَهُ مَرَّتَيْنِ : إِحْدَاهُمَا بِالجُمْلَةِ الاِسْمِيَّةِ، وَالأُخْرَى بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ - تَأَسِّياً بِحَدِيثِ: «إِنَّ الحَمْدَ اللَّهِ نَحْمَدُهُ» - وَجَمْعاً بَيْنَ الأَمْرَيْنِ - أَعْنِي : الحَمْدَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الاِسْمِيَّةِ ، وَالحَمْدَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ - ؛ لِيَشْرَبَ بِكُلِّ مِنَ الكَاسَيْنِ ; أَيْ : لِيُحَصِّلَ ثَوَابَ الحَمْدِ بِكُلِّ مِنَ الجُمْلَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ . وَاخْتَارَ فِي الأَوَّلِ التَّعْبِيرَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الإِسْمِيَّةِ ، وَفِي الثَّانِي التَّعْبِيرَ بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ ; لِمُنَاسَبَةِ المَحْمُودِ عَلَيْهِ فِيهِمَا ، وَبَيَانُ ذَلِكَ : - أَنَّ المَحْمُودَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الأَوَّلِ : الذَّاتُ ، وَهِيَ دَائِمَةٌ مُسْتَمِرَّةٌ، فَيُنَاسِبُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ فِيهِ بِالجُمْلَةِ الإِسْمِيَّةِ المُفِيدَةِ لِلدَّوَامِ وَالِاسْتِمْرَارِ . - وَالمَحْمُودَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الثَّانِي : الإِنْعَامُ ، وَهُوَ مُتَجَدِّدٌ شَيْئاً فَشَيْئاً , فَيُنَاسِبُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ فِيهِ بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ المُفِيدَةِ لِلتَّجَدُّدِ شَيْئاً فَشَيْئاً .
His saying: 'We praise Him...' etc. He only praised Him twice: one with the nominal sentence, and the other with the verbal sentence – following the hadith: 'Indeed, praise belongs to Allah; we praise Him' – and combining the two matters, i.e., praise with the nominal sentence, and praise with the verbal sentence, so that he may drink from both cups, meaning: to obtain the reward of praise from each of the two mentioned sentences. And he chose in the first to express with the nominal sentence, and in the second to express with the verbal sentence, due to the suitability of the object of praise in each. The explanation of that: The object of praise in the first is the Essence, and it is permanent and continuous, so it is fitting to use the nominal sentence which indicates permanence and continuity. And the object of praise in the second is the bestowal (of blessings), and it is renewed little by little, so it is fitting to use the verbal sentence which indicates renewal little by little.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by the commentator Bajuri on the author's opening praise phrase. The author of the matn (al-Sullam al-Munawraq) begins with 'We praise Him...' and the commentator observes that the author praises Allah twice: once with the nominal sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' (implied) and once with the verbal sentence 'nahmaduhu'. The commentator first notes that this follows the example of the hadith 'Inna al-hamda lillah nahmaduhu' (narrated by Muslim and Ibn Majah). Then he explains the purpose: the author combines both forms so that the reader may obtain the reward of praising with both types of sentences – likened to drinking from two cups. Then the commentator delves into the wisdom behind the specific order: the first praise (implied 'al-hamdu lillah') uses a nominal sentence because the object of praise is Allah's Essence (al-dhat), which is eternal and unchanging; the nominal sentence, by its nature, indicates permanence and continuity. The second praise ('nahmaduhu') uses a verbal sentence because the object is the bestowal of blessings (al-in'am), which occurs repeatedly and is renewed moment by moment; the verbal sentence indicates renewal and occurrence. This demonstrates a deep sensitivity to the Arabic language and its rhetorical nuances, showing that the author's choice is not arbitrary but driven by the meanings he intends to convey.

الجملة الفعلية

Key Takeaway
The choice of sentence type (nominal vs. verbal) in praise is not arbitrary but is chosen to match the permanent or renewed nature of the object of praise.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Predominant Usage as a Linguistic Principle
Author defends sentence choice by predominant usage and qualifies rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish predominant usage (ghalabat al-isti'mal) from original linguistic assignment (asl al-wad') in resolving apparent contradictions in Islamic texts and identify when a rule is a dominant rule (aghlabiyyah) rather than absolute.

Core Idea
Predominant usage, not rigid logical rules, governs Arabic linguistic conventions.

This passage from the commentary on the hamdalah defends the use of nominal and verbal sentences by appealing to predominant usage (ghalabat al-isti'mal). It also reconciles a disagreement between the renowned grammarian Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani and common practice by distinguishing between original linguistic assignment and contextual indication. Furthermore, it qualifies the rule that attaching a ruling to a derived term indicates causality, reminding us that such rules are only dominant, not absolute. Understanding these principles sharpens your ability to interpret Islamic texts accurately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the opening line: 'لم خصت الاسمية بالدوام والاستمرار، والفعلية بالتجدد، مع صلاحية كل لكل بالقرائن?' This is an objection: why are nominal and verbal sentences each restricted to specific temporal connotations when context can change them? The objection assumes a logical conflict.
The objection targets the author's choice of sentence types in the hamdalah.
2
Extract the answer based on predominant usage
The answer is 'لغلبة الاستعمال' — due to the predominance of usage. The Arabs predominantly used nominal sentences for stability and verbal sentences for renewal, even though either could be used with context clues. This shows that linguistic convention is not rigid logic but follows customary practice.
Ghalabat al-isti'mal is a key concept in balaghah and usul.
3
Analyze the resolution of the contradiction with Abd al-Qahir
The passage mentions that some claim nominal sentences indicate duration, but Abd al-Qahir said they only indicate predication (nubut). Al-Taftazani resolved this: Abd al-Qahir considered the original linguistic assignment (asl al-wad'), while others considered indication through context clues (qara'in). Thus, no real contradiction.
Asl al-wad' vs. dalalah bi al-qara'in is a fundamental distinction in Arabic semantics.
4
Examine the rule on derived terms and its qualification
An objection is raised: since 'al-hamd' is derived from 'hamd' and the extraction (ikhraj) is the source of derivation, the praise should be for the renewal of extraction, favoring a verbal sentence. The response: the causality is only implicit (bi-iqtida'iha), and the rule is only dominant (aghlabiyyah), not absolute. Thus, the objection fails.
This shows the importance of not over-applying logical rules to language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : لِمَ خُصَّتِ الاسْمِيَّةُ بِالدَّوَامِ وَالاسْتِمْرَارِ، وَالفِعْلِيَّةُ بِالتَّجَدُّدِ، مَعَ صَلَاحِيَّةِ كُلِّ لِكُلِّ بِالقَرَائِنِ؟ أَجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ لِغَلَبَةِ الاِسْتِعْمَالِ الوَاقِعِ فِيهِ. وَمَا ذُكِرَ مِنْ أَنَّ الجُمْلَةَ الاِسْمِيَّةَ تَدُلُّ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ وَالِاسْتِمْرَارِ مُخَالِفٌ لِقَوْلِ الشَّيْخِ عَبْدِ القَاهِرِ : «إِنَّهَا لَا تَدُلُّ إِلَّا عَلَى مُجَرَّدِ النُّبُوتِ»، وَدَفَعَ السَّعْدُ التَّفْتَازَانِيُّ المُخَالَفَةَ : بِأَنَّ الشَّيْخَ نَظَرَ لِأَصْلِ الوَضْعِ، وَغَيْرَهُ نَظَرَ لِلدَّلَالَةِ بِالقَرَائِنِ. وَلَمَّا كَانَتِ الجُمْلَةُ الفِعْلِيَّةُ المُفِيدَةُ لِلتَّجَدُّدِ إِنَّمَا هِيَ خُصُوصُ الجُمْلَةِ المُضَارِعِيَّةِ، عَبَّرَ بِهَا دُونَ الجُمْلَةِ المَاضَوِيَّةِ. لَا يُقَالُ: الحَمْدُ الأَوَّلُ مُعَلَّلٌ بِالإِخْرَاجِ السَّابِقِ لِمَا هُوَ القَاعِدَةُ مِنْ: أَنَّ تَعْلِيقَ الحُكْمِ بِالمُشْتَقِّ أَوْ مَا فِي قُوَّتِهِ يُؤذِنُ بِعِليَّةِ مَا مِنْهُ الاِشْتِقَاقُ، فَيَكُونُ الإِخْرَاجُ المَذْكُورُ هُوَ المَحْمُودُ عَلَيْهِ، وَهُوَ مُتَجَدِّدٌ شَيْئاً فَشَيْئاً، فَيُنَاسِبُ أَنْ يَأْتِي فِيهِ بِالجُمْلَةِ الفِعْلِيَّةِ. لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ بِصَرِيحِ العِبَارَةِ، بَلْ بِاقْتِضَائِهَا فَقَطْ؛ عَلَى أَنَّ القَاعِدَةَ المَذْكُورَةَ أَغْلَبِيَّةٌ.
If it is said: Why is the nominal [sentence] specified for duration and continuity, and the verbal [sentence] for renewal, despite each being permissible for the other through context clues? The answer: That is due to the predominance of usage occurring therein. And what was mentioned—that the nominal sentence indicates duration and continuity—contradicts the statement of Sheikh Abd al-Qahir: 'It indicates only mere predication.' And Sa'd al-Taftazani resolved the contradiction: [saying] that the Sheikh considered the original [linguistic] assignment, while others considered indication through context clues. And since the verbal sentence that conveys renewal is specifically the present-tense sentence, he expressed with it and not the past-tense sentence. It cannot be said: The first 'praise' is conditioned by the preceding 'extraction' because of the rule that 'attaching a ruling to a derived term or what is in its power indicates the causality of that from which the derivation is taken,' as previously established; so the mentioned extraction is that which is praised, and it is renewed little by little, so it would be appropriate to use the verbal sentence for it. [Because] we say: That is not by explicit expression, but only by its implication; moreover, the mentioned rule is only a dominant [rule].
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion on the linguistic choices made in the opening hamdalah of the text. It opens with a hypothetical objection: why are nominal sentences (like 'al-hamdu lillah') used for permanence and verbal sentences (like 'nahmaduhu') for renewal, when each could be used for the other with appropriate context clues? The answer given is that this is due to predominant usage (ghalabat al-isti'mal) among the Arabs. The commentator then addresses a potential conflict: the claim that the nominal sentence indicates duration contradicts Sheikh Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani's view that the nominal sentence only indicates predication (nubut) without any temporal connotation. Al-Taftazani resolves this by distinguishing between the original linguistic assignment (asl al-wad') and the contextual indication (dalalah bi al-qara'in). The former is what Abd al-Qahir considered, while the latter is what allows the nominal sentence to imply duration through common usage. The passage then notes that the verbal sentence used for renewal is specifically the present tense (mudari'), not the past tense, because the past tense indicates completed action (inqita'). Next, the commentator rejects a further objection: that the first 'praise' (al-hamd al-awwal) is conditioned by the preceding 'extraction' (al-ikhraj al-sabiq) based on the rule that attaching a ruling to a derived term or its equivalent indicates causality. If that were the case, the extraction would be the object of praise and it is renewing moment by moment, so a verbal sentence would be more appropriate. The response is that the causality is not explicit (sarih al-ibarah) but only implied (bi-iqtida'iha), and moreover, that rule is only a dominant rule (aghlabiyyah), not an absolute one. Thus the objection collapses. Throughout, the commentator emphasizes that linguistic conventions are based on usage patterns, not rigid logical rules.

Key Terms
الجملة الاسمية
الجملة الفعلية
غلبة الاستعمال
القرينة
المشتق
أصل الوضع

D) Based on context clues

Key Takeaway
Predominant usage and dominant rules, rather than strict logical principles, often guide linguistic and legal interpretations in Islamic sciences.

Parsing a Praise Phrase: Khabar and Istisnaf Bayani
Bajuri's grammatical and interpretive analysis of a praise line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a phrase as a predicate of a deleted subject (khabar li-mubtada' mahdhuuf) and distinguish between 'ummat al-ijaba' and 'ummat al-da'wa' in Arabic scholarly texts.

Core Idea
Grammatical parsing unlocks the precise referent of praise.

In this lesson, we examine how Bajuri unpacks a line of praise from his poem. He identifies the grammatical role of the phrase 'Who specified us...' as a predicate for an implied subject, answering the question 'Who is the Praiseworthy?' He also clarifies that the pronoun 'us' refers either to the believing community or all those called to Islam. This kind of parsing is essential for accurate interpretation in Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase's grammatical role
Read Bajuri's statement: the phrase 'Man khassana...' is a predicate (khabar) for a deleted subject (mubtada' mahdhuuf). Find the evidence in the Arabic text.
The deleted subject is likely 'He' (Allah) from the previous line.
2
Recognize the rhetorical structure: istisnaf bayani
Bajuri says the sentence is an explanatory resumption (istisnaf bayani). This means it answers an implied question: 'Who is the one being praised?'
This connects the new sentence to the previous content.
3
Analyze the pronoun 'نا' (us)
The pronoun in 'specified us' refers to the community. Bajuri gives two possibilities: ummat al-ijaba (the believers who responded) or ummat al-da'wa (all those called, including disbelievers). Understand the difference.
This distinction is important in Islamic theology regarding who is included in the Prophet's mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ خَصَّنَا بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلَا

قَوْلُهُ : (مَنْ خَصَّنَا ... إلخ) خَبَرٌ لِمُبْتَدَأَ مَحْذُوفٍ. وَالجُمْلَةُ مُسْتَأنَفَةٌ اسْتِثْنَافاً بَيَانِياً؛ لِأَنَّهَا سِيقَتْ فِي جَوَابِ سُؤَالٍ؛ تَقْدِيرُهُ: «مَنِ المَحْمُودُ؟». وَالضَّمِيرُ البَارِزُ فِي خَصَّنَا، عَائِدٌ لَنَا مَعَاشِرَ أُمَّةِ الإِجَابَةِ - الَّتِي هِيَ خُصُوصُ المُؤْمِنِينَ، أَوْ أُمَّةِ الدَّعْوَةِ الشَّامِلَةِ لِلكُفَّارِ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ بَعْدَ مَادَّةِ التَّخْصِيصِ ...
Who specified us with the best of those who were sent, and the best of those who attained the highest stations. His saying: 'Who specified us... etc.' is a predicate for a deleted subject. And the sentence is an explanatory resumption; because it is given in answer to a question, the estimation of which is: 'Who is the Praiseworthy?' And the explicit pronoun in 'specified us' refers to us, the community of response - which is specifically the believers, or the community of invitation which includes the disbelievers. And know that after the matter of specification...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and interpretive commentary on the second line of the poet's opening verses. Bajuri explains that the phrase 'Man khassana bi khayri man ursila' (Who specified us with the best of those sent) functions as the predicate (khabar) of a deleted subject (mubtada' mahdhuuf). The implied subject is likely 'He' (Allah) mentioned in the previous line. The sentence is an explanatory resumption (istisnaf bayani) because it is presented as an answer to a possible question: 'Who is the one being praised?' who prays for guidance and then praises the Prophet? The pronoun 'نا' 'us' in 'specified us' refers to the community of response (ummat al-ijaba), meaning the believers, or more broadly the community of invitation (ummat al-da'wa) which includes all those called to Islam, including disbelievers. The commentary ends with a grammatical note that after the action of specification, something is necessarily required, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
خبر لمبتدأ محذوف
استئناف بياني
أمة الإجابة
أمة الدعوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Bajuri identify as the grammatical role of the phrase 'مَنْ خَصَّنَا...'?
A) It is a predicate (khabar) for a deleted subject.
B) It is a direct object.
C) It is an adverb of time.
D) It is a circumstantial phrase.

Key Takeaway
Grammatical analysis of praise phrases reveals the implied subject and clarifies the community being addressed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a line from a classical Arabic poem or prose where a phrase functions as a predicate for a deleted subject. Identify the question it answers and state the implied subject.
?
In a Quranic verse such as 'اهْدِنَا الصِّرَاطَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ' (Surah al-Fatiha), identify the grammatical role of the phrase and explain whether it could be considered an explanatory resumption.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Grammar of Praise: Analyzing 'خَيْر' and 'مَنْ' in the Opening Line
Grammatical analysis of 'خَيْر' and 'مَنْ'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the morphological form 'أفعل تفضيل' and explain how the author's grammatical precision about 'مَنْ' prevents a redundant reading.

Core Idea
Grammatical precision safeguards theological meaning.

The opening of the poem praises the Prophet using the word 'خَيْر' (best). But what exactly does this word mean, and who is being referred to? In this passage, the commentator Al-Bajuri carefully dissects the grammar to ensure that the praise is both accurate and avoids contradiction. Understanding these grammatical moves is essential for anyone who wants to read Islamic texts with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the morphological form of 'خَيْر'
The word 'خَيْر' is identified as a noun of preference ('أفعل تفضيل'). Its original form is 'أَخْيَرُ', but the hamza was dropped for ease. This form indicates comparison or superlative.
In Arabic, 'أفعل تفضيل' is like 'أكبر' or 'أفضل'. Here, 'خَيْر' is irregular.
2
Trace the derivation steps
The author explains the phonetic change: the vowel of the yā' was moved to the preceding silent letter, and the hamza was dropped. This is a common process in Arabic morphology to ease pronunciation.
3
Analyze the reference of 'مَنْ'
The word 'مَنْ' in the phrase 'بخير من قد أرسلا' must refer to a prophet or a human, not specifically a messenger (رسول). Otherwise, the verb 'قد أرسلا' (he was sent) would be redundant if 'مَنْ' already implied a messenger.
This shows how grammar affects meaning: if 'مَنْ' meant 'messenger', then 'قد أرسلا' would be repetitive.
4
Connect grammar to theology
By specifying that 'مَنْ' applies to a prophet or human in general, the author ensures that the line praises the Prophet as the best of all prophetic figures, while still allowing 'قد أرسلا' to add the specific information that he was sent.
This grammatical analysis protects the theological point that the Prophet is the best of all humans and prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ خَصَّنَا بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلَا
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا) «خَيْر»: أَفْعُلُ تَفْضِيل، فَأَصْلُهُ: «أَخْيَرُ» نُقِلَتْ حَرَكَةُ اليَاءِ إِلَى السَّاكِنِ قَبْلَهَا، وَحُذِفَتْ مِنْهُ الهَمْزَةُ تَخْفِيفاً ، وَمَنْ وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى نَبِيٍّ أَوْ إِنْسَانٍ، لَا عَلَى رَسُولٍ؛ لِئَلَّا يَضِيعَ قَوْلُهُ : «قَدْ أُرْسَلَا» .
وَاخْتُلِفَ هَلْ خَيرِيَّتُهُ وَ بِسَبَبِ مَزَايَاهُ أَوْ لَا ، بَلْ بِتَفْضِيلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَهُ؟ وَالثَّانِي هُوَ كَلَامُ أَهْلِ التَّحْقِيقِ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ الكَلَامِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ السَّنُوسِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ صُغْرَى الصُّغُرَى. قَوْلُهُ : (وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا) «مَنْ هُنَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى إِنْسَانٍ»؛ أَعَمُّ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ رَسُولاً أَوْ لَا ، صِفَتُهُ أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ المَرَاتِبَ العَالِيَةَ، فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ. والعُلَا جَمْعُ: «عُلْيَا» - بِالضَّمِّ وَالقَصْرِ ، وَهِيَ كَـ: «العَلْيَاءِ» ـ بِالفَتْحِ وَالمَدِّ - ؛ ضِدُّ : السُّفْلَى.
الأنبابي
قوله : (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) وفي العطف زيادةً على فائدة التَّعميم : الإشارة لردّ ما ذهب إليه الزمخشري من تفضيل جبريل على نبينا وعلى غيره مِنَ الأنبياء عليه وعليهم أفضل الصَّلاة وأتم التسليم.
مَنْ خَصَّنَا بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلَا. Al-Bajuri: His statement: (بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا) - 'خَيْر' is a noun of preference, its original is 'أَخْيَرُ', the movement of the yā was transferred to the preceding quiescent, and the hamza was dropped for ease. And 'من' applies to a prophet or a human, not to a messenger, so that his statement 'قَدْ أُرْسَلَا' would not be wasted. And it is disputed whether his excellence is because of his qualities or rather by the preference of Allah the Exalted? The second is the statement of the people of verification among the imams of kalām, as al-Sanūsī said in his commentary on Ṣughrā al-Ṣughrā. His statement: (وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا) - 'من' here applies to a human, more general than whether it is a messenger or not, his attribute is that he gathered the high ranks, so this is more general than what preceded. And 'العُلَا' is the plural of 'عُلْيَا' - with ḍamma and qaṣr -, and it is like 'العَلْيَاءِ' - with fatḥa and madd -; the opposite of 'السُّفْلَى'. Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) - And in the phrase there is, besides the benefit of generalization, an indication to refute what al-Zamakhsharī went to of the preference of Jibrīl over our Prophet and over other prophets, upon him and them the best prayer and complete greeting.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) on the opening lines of the poem. The author first explains the word 'خَيْر' as a noun of preference ('أَفْعُلُ تَفْضِيل'), noting its derivation from 'أَخْيَرُ' with elision of hamza. He then specifies that 'من' here refers to a prophet or any human, but not specifically a messenger (رسول), because otherwise the phrase 'قَدْ أُرْسَلَا' ('he was sent') would become redundant. He then raises a theological question: is the Prophet's excellence (خيريته) due to his own qualities or solely by Allah's preference? He states that the second view is the position of the people of verification (أهل التحقيق) from the imams of kalām, citing al-Sanūsī. Next, he comments on the second part of the line, explaining that 'من' here is more general, encompassing all humans, and that the phrase indicates the Prophet's gathering of high ranks, which is more general than being merely the best of messengers. The word 'العُلَا' is defined as the plural of 'عُلْيَا' (highness). The super-commentator al-Anbabiy adds that this phrasing also serves to refute al-Zamakhsharī's claim that Jibrīl is superior to the Prophet and other prophets, implying that the explicit mention of generality reaffirms the Prophet's absolute excellence.

Key Terms
خَيْر
أَفْعَل تَفْضِيل
مَنْ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, to what kind of entity does 'مَنْ' in 'بخير من قد أرسلا' refer?
A) A messenger only
B) A prophet or human, not specifically a messenger
C) An angel
D) Any sent being

Key Takeaway
The word 'خَيْر' is a noun of preference, and the grammatical reference of 'مَنْ' must be precise to avoid redundancy and protect theological meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the phrase 'خير المرسلين' (best of messengers) morphologically. Explain why it is also a noun of preference and what it implies about the Prophet's status compared to 'خير من قد أرسلا'.
?
In a creedal statement, a theologian uses the phrase 'خير البشر' (best of humans). Using the analysis from this lesson, determine whether this phrase could be misread to imply something about the Prophet's nature that contradicts Ash'ari theology.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Source of the Prophet's Excellence: Divine Preference vs. Inherent Qualities
Theological dispute on Prophet's excellence and refutation of al-Zamakhshari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Ash'ari position on the source of the Prophet's excellence (tafḍīl) and identify how the super-commentary refutes al-Zamakhshari's view.

Core Idea
The Prophet's excellence is solely by Allah's preference, not earned.

The passage does not only discuss grammar; it also addresses a key theological dispute: Is the Prophet's superiority due to his own qualities or is it purely a gift from Allah? The author sides with the 'people of verification' who hold the latter view. Moreover, a super-commentator uses the text to refute al-Zamakhshari's controversial claim that Jibril is superior to the Prophet. This lesson unpacks these theological nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting views on the Prophet's excellence
The author mentions that it is disputed whether the Prophet's excellence (خيريته) is due to his own qualities (مزاياه) or by Allah's preference (بتفضيل الله).
This is a theological debate within Islam about the basis of ranking prophets.
2
Determine the accepted view according to 'أهل التحقيق'
The author explicitly says the second view (by Allah's preference) is the statement of the people of verification (أهل التحقيق) from the imams of kalām, citing al-Sanūsī.
This aligns with Ash'ari theology that all merit comes from Allah.
3
Analyze the refutation of al-Zamakhshari
Al-Anbabiy notes that the general wording in the second line ('خير من حاز المقامات العلا') not only generalizes but also refutes al-Zamakhshari's claim that Jibril is superior to the Prophet and other prophets.
The generality of 'من' (applying to any human) and the description of gathering high ranks implies the Prophet's absolute excellence.
4
Relate to the principle of divine grace in Ash'ari theology
In Ash'arism, Allah's bestowal of excellence (tafḍīl) is arbitrary and not caused by any inherent quality in the creature. This passage defends that view.
This principle upholds Allah's absolute sovereignty and power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ خَصَّنَا بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلَا
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا) «خَيْر»: أَفْعُلُ تَفْضِيل، فَأَصْلُهُ: «أَخْيَرُ» نُقِلَتْ حَرَكَةُ اليَاءِ إِلَى السَّاكِنِ قَبْلَهَا، وَحُذِفَتْ مِنْهُ الهَمْزَةُ تَخْفِيفاً ، وَمَنْ وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى نَبِيٍّ أَوْ إِنْسَانٍ، لَا عَلَى رَسُولٍ؛ لِئَلَّا يَضِيعَ قَوْلُهُ : «قَدْ أُرْسَلَا» .
وَاخْتُلِفَ هَلْ خَيرِيَّتُهُ وَ بِسَبَبِ مَزَايَاهُ أَوْ لَا ، بَلْ بِتَفْضِيلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَهُ؟ وَالثَّانِي هُوَ كَلَامُ أَهْلِ التَّحْقِيقِ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ الكَلَامِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ السَّنُوسِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ صُغْرَى الصُّغُرَى. قَوْلُهُ : (وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا) «مَنْ هُنَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى إِنْسَانٍ»؛ أَعَمُّ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ رَسُولاً أَوْ لَا ، صِفَتُهُ أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ المَرَاتِبَ العَالِيَةَ، فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ. والعُلَا جَمْعُ: «عُلْيَا» - بِالضَّمِّ وَالقَصْرِ ، وَهِيَ كَـ: «العَلْيَاءِ» ـ بِالفَتْحِ وَالمَدِّ - ؛ ضِدُّ : السُّفْلَى.
الأنبابي
قوله : (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) وفي العطف زيادةً على فائدة التَّعميم : الإشارة لردّ ما ذهب إليه الزمخشري من تفضيل جبريل على نبينا وعلى غيره مِنَ الأنبياء عليه وعليهم أفضل الصَّلاة وأتم التسليم.
مَنْ خَصَّنَا بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلَا. Al-Bajuri: His statement: (بِخَيْرِ مَنْ قَدْ أُرْسِلَا) - 'خَيْر' is a noun of preference, its original is 'أَخْيَرُ', the movement of the yā was transferred to the preceding quiescent, and the hamza was dropped for ease. And 'من' applies to a prophet or a human, not to a messenger, so that his statement 'قَدْ أُرْسَلَا' would not be wasted. And it is disputed whether his excellence is because of his qualities or rather by the preference of Allah the Exalted? The second is the statement of the people of verification among the imams of kalām, as al-Sanūsī said in his commentary on Ṣughrā al-Ṣughrā. His statement: (وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا) - 'من' here applies to a human, more general than whether it is a messenger or not, his attribute is that he gathered the high ranks, so this is more general than what preceded. And 'العُلَا' is the plural of 'عُلْيَا' - with ḍamma and qaṣr -, and it is like 'العَلْيَاءِ' - with fatḥa and madd -; the opposite of 'السُّفْلَى'. Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (فَهَذَا أَعَمُّ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ) - And in the phrase there is, besides the benefit of generalization, an indication to refute what al-Zamakhsharī went to of the preference of Jibrīl over our Prophet and over other prophets, upon him and them the best prayer and complete greeting.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) on the opening lines of the poem. The author first explains the word 'خَيْر' as a noun of preference ('أَفْعُلُ تَفْضِيل'), noting its derivation from 'أَخْيَرُ' with elision of hamza. He then specifies that 'من' here refers to a prophet or any human, but not specifically a messenger (رسول), because otherwise the phrase 'قَدْ أُرْسَلَا' ('he was sent') would become redundant. He then raises a theological question: is the Prophet's excellence (خيريته) due to his own qualities or solely by Allah's preference? He states that the second view is the position of the people of verification (أهل التحقيق) from the imams of kalām, citing al-Sanūsī. Next, he comments on the second part of the line, explaining that 'من' here is more general, encompassing all humans, and that the phrase indicates the Prophet's gathering of high ranks, which is more general than being merely the best of messengers. The word 'العُلَا' is defined as the plural of 'عُلْيَا' (highness). The super-commentator al-Anbabiy adds that this phrasing also serves to refute al-Zamakhsharī's claim that Jibrīl is superior to the Prophet and other prophets, implying that the explicit mention of generality reaffirms the Prophet's absolute excellence.

Key Terms
أَهْل التَّحْقِيق
تَفْضِيل
خَيْرِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the super-commentary by Al-Anbabiy, what additional purpose does the phrase 'وَخَيْرِ مَنْ حَازَ المَقَامَاتِ العُلا' serve?
A) It emphasizes the Prophet's high lineage.
B) It refutes al-Zamakhshari's view that Jibril is superior to the Prophet.
C) It shows the Prophet's excellence is due to his own qualities.
D) It indicates that the Prophet is the best of messengers only.

Key Takeaway
The second line's generality serves to refute al-Zamakhshari's claim of Jibril's superiority, affirming the Prophet's absolute excellence by Allah's preference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the following hypothetical statement: 'He is the best of all beings.' Using the logic of this passage, explain how this statement could be used to refute a claim that a particular angel is superior to the Prophet.
?
In a theological discussion, a student says: 'The Prophet's excellence is due to his own perfect character.' Using the passage, construct a response from the 'people of verification' (أهل التحقيق) that corrects this view.

The Principle of Special After General in the Prophet's Attributes
Author explains the benefit of ordering special after general in the Prophet's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why mentioning the special attribute after the general is rhetorically beneficial and defend this principle against apparent Qur'anic counterexamples.

Core Idea
Special after general adds precision; the reverse is pointless.

In the first line of the matn, the Prophet ﷺ is described as 'al-ʿArabī al-Hāshimī'. Have you wondered why 'al-ʿArabī' (the Arab, more general) comes before 'al-Hāshimī' (the Hashimid, more special)? Al-Bajuri’s commentary explains the elegant arrangement and the rule behind it. This lesson unpacks that rule and shows how he handles a potential objection from the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attributes and their relation
Find the attributes 'al-ʿArabī' and 'al-Hāshimī' in the Arabic. Determine which is more general and which more special. Al-ʿArabī includes all Arabs, while al-Hāshimī is a specific tribe within the Arabs.
2
State the principle: special after general has benefit
Read al-Bajuri’s statement: 'mentioning the special after the general has a benefit, contrary to its opposite'. Understand that the opposite order (general after special) is considered pointless in Arabic rhetoric.
He gives the example 'ālim naḥrīr (learned scholar) where the general 'ālim precedes the more specific naḥrīr.
3
Examine the Qur'anic counterexample
Find the verse 'And he was a messenger, a prophet' (Maryam 51). Here, the attribute 'messenger' comes before 'prophet', which seems to violate the principle of special after general (since messenger is more specific than prophet in some contexts).
4
Analyze the author's response: the grammatical argument
Al-Bajuri argues that 'prophet' (nabiyyan) is a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl), which indicates concomitance with its operator. The order is not a normal attribution but a grammatical structure that conveys simultaneous existence of both prophethood and messengership. Thus, it does not violate the principle.
Note: ḥāl is a grammatical term meaning an adverbial accusative describing the state of the subject.
5
Consider the second response from Ibn al-ʿArabī
Al-Bajuri adds that according to some, 'prophet' and 'messenger' are related by 'general and special in some respect' (umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh), meaning they are not strictly hierarchical. Therefore, the verse is not a valid counterexample.
This shows the depth of the commentary: not only grammatical but also conceptual nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَخْفَى مَا فِي تَقْدِيمِ العَرَبِيِّ عَلَى الهَاشِمِي مِنْ حُسْنِ التَّرْتِيبِ؛ لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ الخَاصِّ بَعْدَ العَامِّ لَهُ فَائِدَةٌ، بِخِلَافِ عَكْسِهِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا فَائِدَةَ لَهُ، وَلِذَلِكَ يَقُولُونَ : عَالِمٌ نَحْرِيرٌ وَلَا يَقُولُونَ : نَحْرِيرٌ عَالِمٌ. وَلَا يَرِدُ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَانَ رَسُولًا نَبِيًّا﴾ [مريم: ٥١]؛ لِأَنَّهُ وَإِنْ ذُكِرَ فِيهِ العَامُ بَعْدَ الخَاصِّ، لَكِنَّهُ قَدْ أَفَادَ مُقَارَنَةَ نُبُوَّتِهِ لِرِسَالَتِهِ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَنَّ نَبِيًّا حَالٌ، وَهِيَ تُفِيدُ المُقَارَنَةَ لِعَامِلِهَا؛ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قَدْ نَقَلَ العَارِفُ الشَّعْرَانِيُّ فِي الكَبْرِيتِ الأَحْمَرِ عَنِ الشَّيْخِ ابْنِ العَرَبِيِّ أَنَّهُ ذَهَبَ فِي فُتُوحَاتِهِ المَكِيَّةِ إِلَى أَنَّهُ يُشْتَرَطُ فِي مُسَمَّى النَّبِيِّ أَنْ يَخْتَصَّ بِأَحْكَامٍ لَا يَشْرُكُهُ فِيهَا قَوْمُهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَيَكُونُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الرَّسُولِ : عُمُومٌ وَخُصُوصٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ ، فَلَا يَكُونُ مِمَّا نَحْنُ فِيهِ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ .
And it is not hidden what is in the precedence of 'al-Arabī' over 'al-Hāshimī' of good arrangement; because mentioning the special after the general has a benefit, contrary to its opposite, for it has no benefit. For this reason they say: 'a learned scholar' and they do not say: 'a scholar learned'. And the verse of Allah Most High, 'And he was a messenger, a prophet' [Maryam: 51] is not a counterexample; for although in it the general is mentioned after the special, it has nevertheless benefited the concomitance of his prophethood with his messengership by virtue of 'a prophet' being a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl), and it (the ḥāl) indicates concomitance with its operator. Moreover, the gnostic al-Shaʿrānī narrated in al-Kibrīt al-Aḥmar from Shaykh Ibn al-ʿArabī that he held in his al-Futūḥāt al-Makkiyya that the requirement for the meaning of 'prophet' is that he be distinguished by rulings in which his people do not share; and upon this, between it (prophet) and 'messenger' there is general and special in some respect (umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh), so it is not from what we are dealing with. So let it be contemplated.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the first line of the matn, explaining the order of the Prophet's attributes. The author, al-Bajuri, states that it is clear why 'al-Arabi' (the Arab) is placed before 'al-Hashimi' (the Hashimid): mentioning the special after the general provides benefit, whereas the reverse gives no benefit. He illustrates this with the common Arabic expression 'a learned scholar' (ʿālim naḥrīr), where the general term 'learned' comes before the more specific 'scholar'. He then addresses a potential objection from the Qur'anic verse 'And he was a messenger, a prophet' (Maryam 51), where 'messenger' (general in some respects) precedes 'prophet' (special). He argues that here the general after the special is justified because 'a prophet' is a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl) that indicates concomitance between the two states. Furthermore, he cites a view from Ibn al-ʿArabī that 'prophet' and 'messenger' are related by 'general and special in some respect', meaning they are not in a strict general-special hierarchy, so the verse does not undermine the principle that the special after the general is preferable.

Key Terms
الخاص
العام
الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why is it better to mention the special attribute after the general attribute?
A) Because the reverse causes confusion in meaning.
B) Because mentioning the special after the general provides additional benefit of specifying the particular quality.
C) Because the general always encompasses the special, so the order does not matter.
D) Because the special is more important and should be emphasized.

Key Takeaway
Al-Bajuri teaches that ordering special after general is rhetorically beneficial, and apparent counterexamples like 'messenger, a prophet' are resolved by grammatical and conceptual analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another example in the Qur'an where a general attribute is followed by a special one (e.g., 'al-ʿAzīz al-Ḥakīm' – the Mighty, the Wise). Explain why the order is rhetorically effective and how it aligns with the principle of special after general.
?
Write a short defense of the principle 'special after general is beneficial' using the grammatical argument of ḥāl, applying it to a different Qur'anic verse that might appear to break the rule.

Virtues of Salawat and the Shaykh Debate
Al-Bajuri enumerates virtues and a debated property of salawat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the role of salawat and the role of a shaykh in spiritual enlightenment versus attaining wilaya, based on al-Bajuri's discussion.

Core Idea
Salawat illuminates hearts but cannot replace the spiritual guide for sainthood.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary not only extols the countless benefits of sending blessings upon the Prophet but also addresses a subtle debate: can salawat substitute for a living spiritual master? Al-Bajuri reports different scholarly opinions, then resolves the issue by distinguishing between general enlightenment and the attainment of wilaya. Understanding this distinction helps you navigate similar debates in Islamic spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claims about salawat's benefits
Read the first part of the passage. Al-Bajuri lists three categories: fulfilment of needs, removal of severe distress, and descent of mercies. Notice the rhetorical style: he says the virtues are too many to enumerate.
This is a common pattern in praise texts.
2
Extract the debated claim about the shaykh
Find the statement that salawat 'suffices instead of the shaykh' and 'takes his place'. Note that this is reported from Zarruq and al-Sanusi, but al-Mallawiy qualifies it.
The debate is about the scope of substitution.
3
Analyze al-Mallawiy's qualification
Al-Mallawiy restricts the substitution to 'mere enlightenment' (tanwir). For 'reaching the level of sainthood' (wilaya), a shaykh remains necessary. Understand the distinction between general spiritual illumination and the specific attainment of walaya.
This shows the precision of later commentators.
4
Compare salawat with other remembrances
Al-Bajuri adds a unique property: salawat extinguishes the 'heat of natures' (base passions), while other remembrances may increase it. Consider why this distinction matters for practice.
This differentiates the effect of salawat from other dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَعَمْ؛ هُوَ خِلَافُ الأَوْلَى قَطعاً . وَالأَحَادِيثُ فِي فَضْل الصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ جَمَّةٌ لَا تَنْضَبِطُ، وَخَصَائِصُهَا لَا تَنْحَصِرُ : - فَمِنْ ذَلِكَ : قَضَاءُ الحَاجَاتِ، وَكَشْفُ الكُرَبِ المُعْضَلَاتِ، وَنُزُولُ الرَّحَمَاتِ. - وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ أَيْضاً : مَا جُرِّبَ مِنْ تَأثِيرِهَا فِي تَنْوِيرِ القُلُوبِ حَتَّى قِيلَ: إِنَّهَا تَكْفِي عَنِ الشَّيْخ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَتَقُومُ مُقَامَهُ، كَمَا حَكَاهُ سَيِّدِي أَحْمَد زَرُّوق وَالشَّيْخُ السَّنُوسِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ صُغْرَى الصُّغُرَى» ، وَأَشَارَ لَهُ الشَّيْخُ أَبُو العَبَّاسِ أَحْمَدُ بْنُ مُوسَى اليَمَنِيُّ ، لَكِنْ قَالَ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ : المُرَادُ أَنَّهَا تَكْفِي عَنْهُ، وَتَقُومُ مَقَامَهُ فِي مُجَرَّدِ التَّنْوِيرِ ، أَمَّا الوُصُولُ لِدَرَجَةِ الوِلَايَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ فِيهِ مِنْ شَيْخِ، كَمَا هُوَ مَعْلُومٌ عِنْدَ أَهْلِهِ ، وَاخْتَصَّتْ مِنْ بَيْنِ الأَذْكَارِ بِأَنَّهَا تُذْهِبُ حَرَارَةَ الطَّبَاعِ، بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِهَا فَإِنَّهُ يُشِيرُهَا .
Yes, it is contrary to what is preferable definitively. The hadiths on the virtue of blessings upon him are numerous and cannot be encompassed, and its special properties cannot be limited. Among them: fulfillment of needs, removal of severe distress, and descent of mercies. And among them also is what has been experienced of its effect in enlightening hearts, to the point that it is said: it suffices instead of the shaykh in the path and takes his place, as related by Sayyidi Ahmad Zarruq and al-Shaykh al-Sanusi in his commentary on al-Sughra al-Sughra, and al-Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Musa al-Yamani indicated it, but al-Shaykh al-Mallawiy said: the intended meaning is that it suffices instead of him and takes his place in mere enlightenment; as for reaching the level of sainthood, a shaykh is necessary, as is known among its people. And it is distinguished among remembrances by extinguishing the heat of natures, unlike others which increase it.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening invocation of the matn. Al-Bajuri affirms that the salawat (blessings on the Prophet) are not merely optional but are superior. He then lists several benefits: fulfilment of needs, removal of severe distress, and descent of mercies. He also discusses a debated point: whether reciting salawat can substitute for a spiritual guide (shaykh) in the path of tasawwuf. He reports that some scholars claim it suffices for enlightenment, but al-Mallawiy clarifies that this is only for general illumination, not for attaining the rank of sainthood (wilaya), which requires a shaykh. Finally, he notes a unique property: salawat extinguishes the heat of base passions, whereas other remembrances may increase it.

Key Terms
الصلاة
الشيخ
التنوير
الولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Mallawiy, in which aspect can salawat substitute for a shaykh?
A) In attaining sainthood (wilaya)
B) In learning the Quran
C) In mere enlightenment (tanwir)
D) In performing Hajj

Key Takeaway
Salawat has immense virtues, but its substitution for a shaykh is limited to general enlightenment; the attainment of wilaya requires a living spiritual guide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the passage again. Identify the specific phrase where al-Mallawiy restricts the substitution. Then, in your own words, write one sentence explaining why a shaykh is still needed for wilaya according to this passage.
?
Consider a similar debate in Usul al-Fiqh: can general principles (like istihsan) replace the need for a specific text? Write a short comparison between that debate and the salawat-shaykh discussion.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
