The Companions as Stars: All Mujtahids?
Commentary on the Companions as stars and their ijtihad status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the apparent meaning of the hadith 'My companions are like stars' as understood by Ibn Hajar and justify the position that all Companions were mujtahids.

Core Idea
The hadith of the Companions as stars is interpreted by Ibn Hajar to prove that all Companions were mujtahids.

In this passage, the commentators explain the line of al-Sullam that likens the Companions to stars for guidance. They cite two hadiths and discuss their implications. The apparent meaning, as held by Ibn Hajar, is that all Companions were qualified mujtahids, not blind followers. This lesson unpacks that claim and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two hadiths
Find the two hadiths cited in the commentary. The first is a qudsi hadith where Allah says the Companions are like stars; the second is the famous 'My companions are like stars, with whichever of them you follow you will be guided.'
The second hadith is the one with authenticity debates.
2
Identify the apparent meaning according to the commentators
The passage states: 'وَظَاهِرُ هَذَيْنِ الحَدِيثَيْنِ : أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كُلَّهُمْ مُجْتَهِدُونَ' – the apparent meaning of these two hadiths is that all Companions are mujtahids.
3
Understand Ibn Hajar's reasoning
Ibn Hajar argued that the conditions of ijtihad were met in all Companions, and therefore none of them followed another blindly. The passage quotes him: 'وَعَلَّلَهُ بِتَوَفِّرِ شُرُوطِ الاِجْتِهَادِ فِي جَمِيعِهِمْ'.
This is a strong claim; later scholars debated it.
4
Consider the objection about taqlid
Some scholars held that there were both mujtahids and muqallids among the Companions. The passage notes: 'لَكِنْ رَبَّحَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّ فِيهِمُ المُقَلِّدِينَ وَالمُجْتَهِدِينَ'.
This shows the question is not settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ ذَوِي الهُدَى مَنْ شُبِّهُوا بِأَنْجُمِ فِي الاهْتِدَا
الباجوري
(1) هَذَا؛ وَفِي بَعْضِ التَّفَاسِيرِ تَفْسِيرُ الهِدَايَةِ فِي الآيَةِ المَذْكُورَةِ بِخَلْقِ الاِهْتِدَاءِ، فَلْيُرَاجَعْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مَنْ شُبِّهوا ... إلخ) أَشَارَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَى مَا رُوِيَ مِنْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَأَلَ الرَّبَّ عَمَّا يَخْتَلِفُ فِيهِ أَصْحَابُهُ، فَقَالَ: «يَا مُحَمَّدُ! أَصْحَابُكَ عِنْدِي كَالنُّجُومِ فِي السَّمَاءِ، بَعْضُهَا أَضْوَءُ مِنْ بَعْضٍ، فَمَنْ أَخَذَ بِشَيْءٍ مِمَّا اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ فَهُوَ عَلَى هَدْيِي» (۳)، وَإِلَى مَا رُوِيَ أَيْضاً مِنْ أَنَّهُ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُومِ، بِأَيْهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ » .
الأنبابي
(٤) المُحَقِّقِينَ: إنَّه لا خلاف بل هي تطلق لغةً بالمعنيين، وفتح باب التأويل لأحد الفريقين دون الآخر خلاف الإنصاف.
قوله : (بِخَلْقِ الاهْتِدَاء) وعلى هذا يكون قوله : (مَنْ أَحْبَبْتُ ﴾ [القصص : ٥٦] لبيان سبب النزول؛ لأنَّها نزلت في عمه أبي طالب، وإلا فنفي الخلف عام . اهـ مؤلّف. قوله : (سَأَلَ الرَّبَّ) أي بلا واسطةٍ ليلة المعراج، ويُحتمل أنه كان بواسطة جبريل، والأوَّلُ أقربُ إلى العبارة.
ثمَّ يُحتمل أن يكون السُّؤال قبل الاختلاف، أو بعده؛ فعلى الأوّل يكون من باب الإخبار بالمغيبات. قوله : (عَمَّا يَخْتَلِفُ) أي : مِن أحكام الدِّين التي للاجتهاد دخل فيها .
قوله : ( فِي السَّمَاءِ) حالٌ مِنَ النُّجوم»، وأتى بها مع أنَّ النُّجوم لا تكون إلا في السَّماء؛ للإشارة إلى علو مرتبة الصَّحابة، كعلو محل النجوم.
قوله : (بَعْضُهَا ... إلخ) حال أيضاً مِنَ النُّجوم»، أتى بها مع عدم توقف جواب السؤال عليها؛ إشارة إلى تفاوت مراتب الصحابة كتفاوت مراتب النُّجوم. قوله : (فَهُوَ عَلَى هَدْي) بفتح الهاء وسكون الدَّال.

الشرشيمي: قوله : (بِخَلْقِ الِاهْتِدَاءِ وعلى ذلك : إنَّما خصَّ مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ ﴾ [القصص: ٥٦] لكونه سبب النُّزول، لا للاحتراز .
الشرشيمي: قوله : (فِي السَّمَاءِ) حالٌ مِنَ النُّجُوم» أفاد علو المرتبة . وقوله : (بَعْضُهَا أَضْوَءُ مِنْ بَعْضِ حال ثانيةٌ أفادت تفاوت مرتبتهم ، وإن لم يتوقف عليه الجواب ؛ لأنَّ اختلافهم في الاجتهاد، وفي الدَّلالة مأخوذ من تشبيههم بالنُّجوم؛ لتفاوت المهتدين في الجهات والنواحي.

وَظَاهِرُ هَذَيْنِ الحَدِيثَيْنِ : أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كُلَّهُمْ مُجْتَهِدُونَ، وَهُوَ مَا جَرَى عَلَيْهِ ابْنُ حَجَرَ فِي شَرْحِ الهَمْزِيَّةِ ، وَعَلَّلَهُ بِتَوَفِّرِ شُرُوطِ الاِجْتِهَادِ فِي جَمِيعِهِمْ؛ قَالَ: وَلِذَلِكَ لَمْ يُعْرَف أَنَّ وَاحِداً مِنْهُمْ قَلَّدَ غَيْرَهُ فِي مَسْأَلَةٍ مِنَ المَسَائِلِ (۱) ، لَكِنْ رَبَّحَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّ فِيهِمُ المُقَلِّدِينَ (۲) وَالمُجْتَهِدِينَ . ثُمَّ إِنَّ بَعْضَهُمْ تَكَلَّمَ فِي سَنَدِ الحَدِيثِ الثَّانِي حَتَّى قَالَ الشَّهَابُ فِي شَرْحِ الشَّفَا»: «إِنَّهُ رُوِيَ مِنْ طُرُقٍ كُلُّهَا ضَعِيفَةٌ (۳)، بَلْ قَالَ ابْنُ حَزْمٍ: «إِنَّهُ مَوْضُوعٌ (٤)، لَكِنْ نَقَلَ العَارِفُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى الشَّعْرَانِيُّ فِي المِيزَانِ أَنَّهُ صَحِيحٌ عِنْدَ أَهْلِ الكَشْفِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِ مَقَالٌ ( ٥ ) .
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : خِطَابُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : بِأَيْهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرٌ، وَلَا لِغَيْرِهِمْ؛ لِعَدَمِ حُضُورِهِمْ حِينَ الخِطَابِ . أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ لِغَيْرِهِمْ عَلَى طَرِيقِ اسْتِحْضَارِهِمْ وَفَرْضِهِمْ حَاضِرِينَ؛ كَذَا قَالَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ (٦)، ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ أَنَّ الشَّيْخَ تَقِي الدِّينِ السُّبْكِي نَقَلَ عَنْ تَاجِ الدِّينِ بْنِ عَطَاءِ اللَّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَتْ لَهُ تَجَلِّيَاتُ يَرَى فِي بَعْضِهَا سَائِرَ أُمَّتِهِ الآتِيَةَ بَعْدَهُ، فَيَقُولُ مُخَاطِبَاً لَهُمْ: لَا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِي فَوَ الَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَوْ أَنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ أَنْفَقَ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَبًا مَا أَدْرَكَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ» (۷)، قَالَ : وَمِثْلُهُ يُقَالُ فِي الخِطَابِ الَّذِي نَحْنُ بِصَدَدِهِ. اهـ (۸).
الأنبابي: قوله : (لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرٌ) أي : لأنَّهم كلُّهم مجتهدون؛ بناء على ما جرى عليه ابن حجر .
(8) And his family and his companions, possessors of guidance, who are likened to stars in guidance.
Al-Bajuri: (1) This; and in some commentaries, the interpretation of 'guidance' in the mentioned verse is by creating the guidance, so let it be consulted. His statement: 'who are likened ... etc.' alluded by that to what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked the Lord about what his companions differ in, so He said: 'O Muhammad! Your companions with Me are like stars in the sky, some of them are brighter than others, so whoever takes something from what they differed in is upon My guidance' (3), and to what is also narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'My companions are like stars; with whichever of them you follow you will be guided.'
Al-Anbabi: (4) The verifiers: there is no disagreement; rather it is used linguistically in both meanings, and opening the door of interpretation for one of the two groups without the other is contrary to fairness.
His statement: 'by creating the guidance' - and on this, His statement: 'Whom you love' [Qasas 28:56] is to indicate the cause of revelation; because it was revealed about his uncle Abu Talib, else negation of failure is general. End of author. His statement: 'he asked the Lord' - meaning without an intermediary on the night of Mi'raj, and it is possible that it was through Jibril, and the first is closer to the expression. Then it is possible that the question was before the difference, or after; on the first it would be from the category of informing of unseen matters. His statement: 'about what they differ' - meaning from the rulings of the religion in which ijtihad has an entry. His statement: 'in the sky' is a circumstantial qualifier from 'the stars', and he brought it even though stars are only in the sky; to indicate the high rank of the Companions, like the high place of stars. His statement: 'some of them ... etc.' is also an circumstantial qualifier from 'the stars', he brought it despite the answer to the question not depending on it; indicating the difference in ranks of the Companions like the difference in ranks of stars. His statement: 'so he is upon guidance' - with fatha on ha and sukun on dal.
Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'by creating the guidance' and on that: He specified 'Whom you love' [Qasas 28:56] because it is a cause of revelation, not for restriction. Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'in the sky' is a circumstantial from 'the stars', it gives the meaning of high rank. And his statement: 'some of them are brighter than others' is a second circumstantial, indicating the variance of their rank, even if the answer does not depend on it; because their difference in ijtihad and in indication is taken from comparing them to stars; due to the variance of those guided in directions and regions.
And the apparent meaning of these two hadiths is that all the Companions are mujtahids, and this is what Ibn Hajar followed in his commentary on al-Hamziyya, and he gave the reason as the availability of the conditions of ijtihad in all of them. He said: For that reason it is not known that any of them followed another in a single issue. But some of them preferred that among them are muqallids and mujtahids. Then some of them spoke about the chain of the second hadith, even al-Shihab said in his commentary on al-Shifa: 'It was narrated through paths all of which are weak,' rather Ibn Hazm said: 'It is fabricated,' but al-Sha'rani, the knower of Allah the Exalted, transmitted in al-Mizan that it is authentic according to the people of kashf, even though there is discussion about it. (5)
If it is said: His address in his statement: 'By whichever of them you follow you will be guided' is not valid to be to the Companions as is apparent, nor to others because of their absence at the time of address. The answer: It is to others on the way of bringing them to mind and supposing them present; thus said some of the verifiers (6), then he mentioned that al-Subki transmitted from Taj al-Din ibn 'Ata'illah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) had manifestations in which he saw the rest of his nation coming after him, so he would address them saying: 'Do not curse my Companions, for by the One in whose hand is my soul, if one of you were to spend the equivalent of Uhud in gold, he would not reach the mudd of one of them nor its half.' (7) He said: And similar is said about the address we are dealing with. End. (8)
Al-Anbabi: His statement: 'It is not valid to be to the Companions as is apparent' - meaning because they are all mujtahids, based on what Ibn Hajar followed.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of al-Sullam al-Munawraq that likens the Prophet's family and companions to stars for guidance. The commentators explain the meaning of the line, cite relevant hadith, and address scholarly discussions about the status of the Companions.

The commentary begins with al-Bajuri noting that in some tafsirs, 'guidance' in the verse is interpreted as the creation of guidance. Then he explains that the phrase 'who are likened' refers to a hadith in which the Prophet asked Allah about the differences among his Companions, and Allah replied that they are like stars, some brighter than others, and whoever follows any of them is upon guidance. A second hadith also states that the Companions are like stars and following any of them leads to guidance.

Al-Anbabi then comments on a point about the interpretation of guidance, clarifying that there is no disagreement; the term is used in both senses linguistically. He elaborates on the hadith, explaining that the Prophet's question to Allah was without intermediary on the night of Mi'raj, and that the question could have been before or after the differences occurred. He also explains the grammar of the hadith, noting that 'in the sky' indicates the high rank of the Companions, and 'some of them brighter than others' indicates their varying ranks.

Al-Shirshimi adds marginal notes, emphasizing that the specification of the verse about Abu Talib is due to the cause of revelation, not a restriction, and that the description of the stars as being in the sky and varying in brightness signifies high rank and variance in merit, which is why differences in ijtihad are permissible.

The commentary then discusses the apparent meaning of the two hadiths: that all Companions are mujtahids. Ibn Hajar held this view, arguing that the conditions of ijtihad were met in all of them, and therefore no Companion was seen to blindly follow another. However, some scholars preferred that among them were both muqallids and mujtahids. Then follows a discussion on the authenticity of the second hadith: al-Shihab considered its chains weak, Ibn Hazm declared it fabricated, but al-Sha'rani said it is authentic according to the people of kashf (mystical unveiling).

The final section addresses a question: to whom is the address 'By whichever of them you follow you will be guided' directed? It cannot be to the Companions themselves because they were present, nor to others who were absent. The answer is that it is directed to later generations by way of bringing the Companions to mind and supposing them present. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet addressed later generations not to curse his Companions. Thus, the address in the hadith about following the Companions is validly applied to later Muslims.

The passage concludes with al-Anbabi reiterating that the address cannot be to the Companions because they are all mujtahids, following Ibn Hajar's position.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was Ibn Hajar's reason for claiming that all Companions were mujtahids?
A) Because the hadith explicitly says so.
B) Because the conditions of ijtihad were met in all of them.
C) Because no Companion ever disagreed with another.
D) Because the Companions were all prophets.

Key Takeaway
The apparent meaning of the 'stars' hadith is that all Companions are mujtahids, but this is debated, highlighting the importance of understanding ijtihad and taqlid in evaluating their legal authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Based on the passage, reconstruct Ibn Hajar's argument that all Companions were mujtahids. Identify the premise that the conditions of ijtihad were met in all of them, and the conclusion that no Companion blindly followed another.
?
Consider a hypothetical scenario: If a student of knowledge encounters a ruling attributed to a Companion that contradicts a ruling from another Companion, how would the position of Ibn Hajar help resolve the apparent conflict? Use the passage to answer.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
12 min
Debating the Hadith's Authenticity and Address
Debate on the hadith's authenticity and its addressee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the scholarly positions on the authenticity of the hadith 'My companions are like stars' and explain the justification for its address to later generations.

Core Idea
Despite weak chains, the hadith is defended by kashf, and its address to later Muslims is justified by imagining the Companions present.

The passage continues by examining the second hadith's authenticity. Some scholars declared its chains weak or even fabricated, while al-Sha'rani defended it through mystical unveiling (kashf). Then a dialectical question is raised: to whom is the address directed? The answer draws on a similar hadith about not cursing the Companions, showing that the Prophet addressed later generations as if they were present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criticisms of the hadith's chain
The passage mentions that al-Shihab said the hadith was narrated through weak paths, and Ibn Hazm declared it fabricated.
These are strong criticisms from hadith scholars.
2
Note al-Sha'rani's defense
Al-Sha'rani, using kashf (mystical unveiling), claimed the hadith is authentic according to the people of kashf, despite external criticism.
This is an epistemological claim based on inner knowledge.
3
Understand the objection about the addressee
The objection: the address 'By whichever of them you follow' cannot be to the Companions (they were present) nor to others (they were absent). So how is it valid?
This is a logical problem about the speech act.
4
Learn the answer: address to later generations through mental presence
The answer: the address is to later Muslims, with the Companions mentally brought to mind and supposed present. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet addressed later generations not to curse his Companions.
This uses the principle of istihdar (bringing to mind).

(۸) وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ ذَوِي الهُدَى مَنْ شُبِّهُوا بِأَنْجُمِ فِي الاهْتِدَا
الباجوري
(1) هَذَا؛ وَفِي بَعْضِ التَّفَاسِيرِ تَفْسِيرُ الهِدَايَةِ فِي الآيَةِ المَذْكُورَةِ بِخَلْقِ الاِهْتِدَاءِ، فَلْيُرَاجَعْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مَنْ شُبِّهوا ... إلخ) أَشَارَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَى مَا رُوِيَ مِنْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَأَلَ الرَّبَّ عَمَّا يَخْتَلِفُ فِيهِ أَصْحَابُهُ، فَقَالَ: «يَا مُحَمَّدُ! أَصْحَابُكَ عِنْدِي كَالنُّجُومِ فِي السَّمَاءِ، بَعْضُهَا أَضْوَءُ مِنْ بَعْضٍ، فَمَنْ أَخَذَ بِشَيْءٍ مِمَّا اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ فَهُوَ عَلَى هَدْيِي» (۳)، وَإِلَى مَا رُوِيَ أَيْضاً مِنْ أَنَّهُ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُومِ، بِأَيْهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ » .
الأنبابي
(٤) المُحَقِّقِينَ: إنَّه لا خلاف بل هي تطلق لغةً بالمعنيين، وفتح باب التأويل لأحد الفريقين دون الآخر خلاف الإنصاف.
قوله : (بِخَلْقِ الاهْتِدَاء) وعلى هذا يكون قوله : (مَنْ أَحْبَبْتُ ﴾ [القصص : ٥٦] لبيان سبب النزول؛ لأنَّها نزلت في عمه أبي طالب، وإلا فنفي الخلف عام . اهـ مؤلّف. قوله : (سَأَلَ الرَّبَّ) أي بلا واسطةٍ ليلة المعراج، ويُحتمل أنه كان بواسطة جبريل، والأوَّلُ أقربُ إلى العبارة.
ثمَّ يُحتمل أن يكون السُّؤال قبل الاختلاف، أو بعده؛ فعلى الأوّل يكون من باب الإخبار بالمغيبات. قوله : (عَمَّا يَخْتَلِفُ) أي : مِن أحكام الدِّين التي للاجتهاد دخل فيها .
قوله : ( فِي السَّمَاءِ) حالٌ مِنَ النُّجوم»، وأتى بها مع أنَّ النُّجوم لا تكون إلا في السَّماء؛ للإشارة إلى علو مرتبة الصَّحابة، كعلو محل النجوم.
قوله : (بَعْضُهَا ... إلخ) حال أيضاً مِنَ النُّجوم»، أتى بها مع عدم توقف جواب السؤال عليها؛ إشارة إلى تفاوت مراتب الصحابة كتفاوت مراتب النُّجوم. قوله : (فَهُوَ عَلَى هَدْي) بفتح الهاء وسكون الدَّال.

الشرشيمي: قوله : (بِخَلْقِ الِاهْتِدَاءِ وعلى ذلك : إنَّما خصَّ مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ ﴾ [القصص: ٥٦] لكونه سبب النُّزول، لا للاحتراز .
الشرشيمي: قوله : (فِي السَّمَاءِ) حالٌ مِنَ النُّجُوم» أفاد علو المرتبة . وقوله : (بَعْضُهَا أَضْوَءُ مِنْ بَعْضِ حال ثانيةٌ أفادت تفاوت مرتبتهم ، وإن لم يتوقف عليه الجواب ؛ لأنَّ اختلافهم في الاجتهاد، وفي الدَّلالة مأخوذ من تشبيههم بالنُّجوم؛ لتفاوت المهتدين في الجهات والنواحي.

وَظَاهِرُ هَذَيْنِ الحَدِيثَيْنِ : أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كُلَّهُمْ مُجْتَهِدُونَ، وَهُوَ مَا جَرَى عَلَيْهِ ابْنُ حَجَرَ فِي شَرْحِ الهَمْزِيَّةِ ، وَعَلَّلَهُ بِتَوَفِّرِ شُرُوطِ الاِجْتِهَادِ فِي جَمِيعِهِمْ؛ قَالَ: وَلِذَلِكَ لَمْ يُعْرَف أَنَّ وَاحِداً مِنْهُمْ قَلَّدَ غَيْرَهُ فِي مَسْأَلَةٍ مِنَ المَسَائِلِ (۱) ، لَكِنْ رَبَّحَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّ فِيهِمُ المُقَلِّدِينَ (۲) وَالمُجْتَهِدِينَ . ثُمَّ إِنَّ بَعْضَهُمْ تَكَلَّمَ فِي سَنَدِ الحَدِيثِ الثَّانِي حَتَّى قَالَ الشَّهَابُ فِي شَرْحِ الشَّفَا»: «إِنَّهُ رُوِيَ مِنْ طُرُقٍ كُلُّهَا ضَعِيفَةٌ (۳)، بَلْ قَالَ ابْنُ حَزْمٍ: «إِنَّهُ مَوْضُوعٌ (٤)، لَكِنْ نَقَلَ العَارِفُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى الشَّعْرَانِيُّ فِي المِيزَانِ أَنَّهُ صَحِيحٌ عِنْدَ أَهْلِ الكَشْفِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِ مَقَالٌ ( ٥ ) .
فَإِنْ قِيلَ : خِطَابُهُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : بِأَيْهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرٌ، وَلَا لِغَيْرِهِمْ؛ لِعَدَمِ حُضُورِهِمْ حِينَ الخِطَابِ . أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ لِغَيْرِهِمْ عَلَى طَرِيقِ اسْتِحْضَارِهِمْ وَفَرْضِهِمْ حَاضِرِينَ؛ كَذَا قَالَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ (٦)، ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ أَنَّ الشَّيْخَ تَقِي الدِّينِ السُّبْكِي نَقَلَ عَنْ تَاجِ الدِّينِ بْنِ عَطَاءِ اللَّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَتْ لَهُ تَجَلِّيَاتُ يَرَى فِي بَعْضِهَا سَائِرَ أُمَّتِهِ الآتِيَةَ بَعْدَهُ، فَيَقُولُ مُخَاطِبَاً لَهُمْ: لَا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِي فَوَ الَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَوْ أَنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ أَنْفَقَ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَبًا مَا أَدْرَكَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ» (۷)، قَالَ : وَمِثْلُهُ يُقَالُ فِي الخِطَابِ الَّذِي نَحْنُ بِصَدَدِهِ. اهـ (۸).
الأنبابي: قوله : (لَا يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِلصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرٌ) أي : لأنَّهم كلُّهم مجتهدون؛ بناء على ما جرى عليه ابن حجر .
(8) And his family and his companions, possessors of guidance, who are likened to stars in guidance.
Al-Bajuri: (1) This; and in some commentaries, the interpretation of 'guidance' in the mentioned verse is by creating the guidance, so let it be consulted. His statement: 'who are likened ... etc.' alluded by that to what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked the Lord about what his companions differ in, so He said: 'O Muhammad! Your companions with Me are like stars in the sky, some of them are brighter than others, so whoever takes something from what they differed in is upon My guidance' (3), and to what is also narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'My companions are like stars; with whichever of them you follow you will be guided.'
Al-Anbabi: (4) The verifiers: there is no disagreement; rather it is used linguistically in both meanings, and opening the door of interpretation for one of the two groups without the other is contrary to fairness.
His statement: 'by creating the guidance' - and on this, His statement: 'Whom you love' [Qasas 28:56] is to indicate the cause of revelation; because it was revealed about his uncle Abu Talib, else negation of failure is general. End of author. His statement: 'he asked the Lord' - meaning without an intermediary on the night of Mi'raj, and it is possible that it was through Jibril, and the first is closer to the expression. Then it is possible that the question was before the difference, or after; on the first it would be from the category of informing of unseen matters. His statement: 'about what they differ' - meaning from the rulings of the religion in which ijtihad has an entry. His statement: 'in the sky' is a circumstantial qualifier from 'the stars', and he brought it even though stars are only in the sky; to indicate the high rank of the Companions, like the high place of stars. His statement: 'some of them ... etc.' is also an circumstantial qualifier from 'the stars', he brought it despite the answer to the question not depending on it; indicating the difference in ranks of the Companions like the difference in ranks of stars. His statement: 'so he is upon guidance' - with fatha on ha and sukun on dal.
Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'by creating the guidance' and on that: He specified 'Whom you love' [Qasas 28:56] because it is a cause of revelation, not for restriction. Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'in the sky' is a circumstantial from 'the stars', it gives the meaning of high rank. And his statement: 'some of them are brighter than others' is a second circumstantial, indicating the variance of their rank, even if the answer does not depend on it; because their difference in ijtihad and in indication is taken from comparing them to stars; due to the variance of those guided in directions and regions.
And the apparent meaning of these two hadiths is that all the Companions are mujtahids, and this is what Ibn Hajar followed in his commentary on al-Hamziyya, and he gave the reason as the availability of the conditions of ijtihad in all of them. He said: For that reason it is not known that any of them followed another in a single issue. But some of them preferred that among them are muqallids and mujtahids. Then some of them spoke about the chain of the second hadith, even al-Shihab said in his commentary on al-Shifa: 'It was narrated through paths all of which are weak,' rather Ibn Hazm said: 'It is fabricated,' but al-Sha'rani, the knower of Allah the Exalted, transmitted in al-Mizan that it is authentic according to the people of kashf, even though there is discussion about it. (5)
If it is said: His address in his statement: 'By whichever of them you follow you will be guided' is not valid to be to the Companions as is apparent, nor to others because of their absence at the time of address. The answer: It is to others on the way of bringing them to mind and supposing them present; thus said some of the verifiers (6), then he mentioned that al-Subki transmitted from Taj al-Din ibn 'Ata'illah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) had manifestations in which he saw the rest of his nation coming after him, so he would address them saying: 'Do not curse my Companions, for by the One in whose hand is my soul, if one of you were to spend the equivalent of Uhud in gold, he would not reach the mudd of one of them nor its half.' (7) He said: And similar is said about the address we are dealing with. End. (8)
Al-Anbabi: His statement: 'It is not valid to be to the Companions as is apparent' - meaning because they are all mujtahids, based on what Ibn Hajar followed.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of al-Sullam al-Munawraq that likens the Prophet's family and companions to stars for guidance. The commentators explain the meaning of the line, cite relevant hadith, and address scholarly discussions about the status of the Companions.

The commentary begins with al-Bajuri noting that in some tafsirs, 'guidance' in the verse is interpreted as the creation of guidance. Then he explains that the phrase 'who are likened' refers to a hadith in which the Prophet asked Allah about the differences among his Companions, and Allah replied that they are like stars, some brighter than others, and whoever follows any of them is upon guidance. A second hadith also states that the Companions are like stars and following any of them leads to guidance.

Al-Anbabi then comments on a point about the interpretation of guidance, clarifying that there is no disagreement; the term is used in both senses linguistically. He elaborates on the hadith, explaining that the Prophet's question to Allah was without intermediary on the night of Mi'raj, and that the question could have been before or after the differences occurred. He also explains the grammar of the hadith, noting that 'in the sky' indicates the high rank of the Companions, and 'some of them brighter than others' indicates their varying ranks.

Al-Shirshimi adds marginal notes, emphasizing that the specification of the verse about Abu Talib is due to the cause of revelation, not a restriction, and that the description of the stars as being in the sky and varying in brightness signifies high rank and variance in merit, which is why differences in ijtihad are permissible.

The commentary then discusses the apparent meaning of the two hadiths: that all Companions are mujtahids. Ibn Hajar held this view, arguing that the conditions of ijtihad were met in all of them, and therefore no Companion was seen to blindly follow another. However, some scholars preferred that among them were both muqallids and mujtahids. Then follows a discussion on the authenticity of the second hadith: al-Shihab considered its chains weak, Ibn Hazm declared it fabricated, but al-Sha'rani said it is authentic according to the people of kashf (mystical unveiling).

The final section addresses a question: to whom is the address 'By whichever of them you follow you will be guided' directed? It cannot be to the Companions themselves because they were present, nor to others who were absent. The answer is that it is directed to later generations by way of bringing the Companions to mind and supposing them present. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet addressed later generations not to curse his Companions. Thus, the address in the hadith about following the Companions is validly applied to later Muslims.

The passage concludes with al-Anbabi reiterating that the address cannot be to the Companions because they are all mujtahids, following Ibn Hajar's position.

Key Terms
الحديث
السند
الكشف
الاستحضار

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the response to the objection that the address in the hadith could not be to the Companions nor to later generations?
A) The hadith is fabricated so the objection is irrelevant.
B) It is addressed to later generations by bringing the Companions to mind and supposing them present.
C) It is addressed to the Companions as if they were absent.
D) The objection is based on a misunderstanding of Arabic grammar.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'My companions are like stars' is defended by kashf and its address to later Muslims is justified through the principle of mental presence, demonstrating the interplay of hadith criticism, theology, and hermeneutics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Linguistic Derivation of 'Amma Ba'd' and 'Wa Ba'd'
Author explains the origin and grammatical structure of 'amma ba'd' and 'wa ba'd'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the linguistic derivation of the phrase 'amma ba'd' from its conditional origin and identify the two main views on the substitution of the waw in 'wa ba'd'.

Core Idea
The phrase 'amma ba'd' is a compressed conditional, and its variant 'wa ba'd' involves a debated substitution of the letter waw.

In the matn, the author uses the phrase 'wa ba'd' (and after) as a transitional marker. But where does this phrase come from? In this lesson, we will unpack al-Bajuri's commentary to understand the original conditional construction behind 'amma ba'd', the deletion and substitution processes that produced it, and the scholarly debate over whether the waw in 'wa ba'd' replaces 'amma' or acts as a simple conjunction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original conditional construction
Find the phrase 'mahma yakun min shay'in ba'd' in the Arabic. Recognize that this is a conditional sentence: 'mahma' (whatever) is the conditional particle, 'yakun' (is) is the verb, 'min shay'in' (some thing) is the subject, and 'ba'd' (after) is the adverb.
The original form explicitly states 'whatever thing is after', which is a complete conditional.
2
Understand the deletion process
Notice that the well-known explanation says the conditional elements (mahma, yakun, min shay'in) were deleted, and 'amma' was brought as a substitute. Understand that this is not a literal deletion after pronunciation, but a structural analysis: the intended meaning is condensed into 'amma ba'd'.
The author clarifies that the deletion is not historical but a linguistic description of the relationship between the two forms.
3
Examine the substitution of 'amma' for 'mahma'
According to the verified view (al-tahqiq), 'amma' substitutes only for 'mahma', not for the whole phrase. The noun after 'amma' (like 'ba'd') serves as compensation (al-iwad) for the deleted verb. Find where al-Bajuri cites Ibn al-Hajib to support this.
Ibn al-Hajib states that they committed to deleting the verb and placing something between 'amma' and its answer as a substitute for the verb.
4
Analyze the variant 'wa ba'd' and the debate over the waw
The matn uses 'wa ba'd' instead of 'amma ba'd'. The author presents two views: (1) the well-known view says the waw substitutes for 'amma', so it is a replacement particle; (2) another view says the waw is a coordinating conjunction and 'amma' is omitted, indicated by the fa' later. Note al-Sakkaki's usage combining both.
The debate hinges on whether the waw is a substitute (niyaba) or a conjunction ('atf). The author implies the well-known view is more accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الناظم (9) وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِلِلِّسَانِ. الباجوري: قَوْلُهُ : (وَبَعْدُ) أَصْلُ هَذِهِ الكَلِمَةِ : «أَمَّا بَعْدُ، وَالأَصْلُ الأَصِيلِ : «مَهْمَا يَكُنْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ بَعْدُ»، فَحُذِفَ كُلٌّ مِنْ مَهْمَا وَيَكُنْ وَمِنْ شَيْءٍ ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّ التَّرْكِيبَ حَقُّهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَكَذَا، وَلَمْ يُوْتَ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الأَمْرِ ، لَا أَنَّهُ نُطِقَ بِهِ ثُمَّ حُذِفَ وَأُتِيَ بِـ «أَمَّا» نِيَابَةً عَنْهُ، فَصَارَ التَّرْكِيبُ : «أَمَّا بَعْدُ» كَذَا اشْتُهِرَ. لَكِنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ أَمَّا لَمْ تَنُبْ إِلَّا عَنْ مَهمَا كَمَا بَحَثَهُ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ؛ قَالَ: وَفِي كَلَامِ ابْنِ الحَاجِبِ مَا يُؤيِّدُهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَالِاسْمُ الَّذِي بَعْدَهَا كَالعِوَضِ مِنَ الفِعْلِ، كَمَا يُصَرِّحُ بِهِ كَلَامُ ابْنِ الحَاجِبِ وَنَصُّهُ : وَالتَزَمُوا حَذْفَ الفِعْلِ بَعْدَهَا - يَعْنِي : «أَمَّا » - ، وَالتَزَمُوا أَنْ يَقَعَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ جَوَابِهَا مَا هُوَ كَالعِوَضِ مِنَ الفِعْلِ المَحْذُوفِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ بَعْضَهُمْ يُعَبِّرُ بِلَفْظِ : «أَمَّا بَعْدُ وَهُوَ السُّنَّةُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كَانَ يَأْتِي بِهِ فِي خُطَبِهِ وَمُرَاسَلَاتِهِ حَتَّى رَوَاهُ بَعْضُ الحُفَّاظ عَنْ أَرْبَعِينَ صَحَابِيًّا، وَبَعْضَهُمْ يُعَبِّرُ بِلَفْظِ : وَبَعْدُ كَمَا هُنَا، فَيَكُونُ قَدْ حَذَفَ أَمَّا وَأَتَى بـ «الوَاوِ» نِيَابَةٌ عَنْهَا ، فَـ الواو فِي هَذَا التَّرْكِيبِ نَائِبَةٌ عَنْ أَمَّا » ؛ هَذَا هُوَ المَشْهُورُ . وَقِيلَ : إِنَّهَا عَاطِفَةٌ، وَأَمَّا مَحْذُوفَةٌ لِدَلَالَةِ الفَاءِ عَلَيْهَا ، وَكَأَنَّ السَّكَاكِيَّ جَرَى عَلَيْهِ فِي المِفْتَاحِ حَيْثُ قَالَ: «وَأَمَّا بَعْدُ» فَجَمَعَ بَيْنَ الوَاءِ و«أَمَّا » ؛ لِكَوْنِهَا لَيْسَتْ نَائِبَةً عَنْهَا . وَالطَّرْفُ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى الضَّمِّ؛
Introduction of the poet: (9) And after: logic is to the heart as grammar is to the tongue. al-Bajuri: His saying: 'And after' – the origin of this word is 'amma ba'd', and the original origin is 'mahma yakun min shay'in ba'd', then each of 'mahma', 'yakun', and 'min shay'in' was deleted, meaning that the construction should have been like that, and nothing of that was brought from the beginning, not that it was spoken then deleted and 'amma' was brought as a substitute for it, so the construction became 'amma ba'd' – this is what is well-known. However, the verified view is that 'amma' only substitutes for 'mahma' as some researchers investigated; he said: and in Ibn al-Hajib's words there is support for it, and accordingly the noun after it is like a substitute for the verb, as is clarified by Ibn al-Hajib's words, his text: 'They committed to deleting the verb after it – meaning 'amma' – and they committed that between it and its answer there should be something that is like a substitute for the deleted verb.' Then some express it as 'amma ba'd' and that is the sunnah, because he (the Prophet) used to use it in his sermons and letters until some memorizers narrated it from forty Companions, and some express it as 'wa ba'd' – as here – so one has deleted 'amma' and brought the waw as a substitute for it, so the waw in this construction is a substitute for 'amma'; this is the well-known view. And it is said: it is a coordinating conjunction, and 'amma' is deleted due to the indication of the fa' on it, and it seems that al-Sakkaki followed this in al-Miftah when he said 'wa amma ba'd' combining the waw and 'amma' because it is not a substitute for it. And the adverb is built on the dammah.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical commentary on the introductory phrase 'wa ba'd' (and after) that appears in the matn. The author first presents the well-known origin: the original phrase is 'mahma yakun min shay'in ba'd' (whatever thing is after), which is a conditional sentence. Through deletion and substitution, it became 'amma ba'd'. The author then mentions two views on how 'amma' replaces the conditional elements. The preferred view is that 'amma' substitutes only for 'mahma', and the noun after it (like 'ba'd') serves as compensation for the deleted verb. Ibn al-Hajib's statement is cited in support. Next, the author discusses the variant 'wa ba'd', used here in the matn. Some, following the Prophet's practice, use 'amma ba'd'. Others replace 'amma' with the waw, making the waw a substitute. A different opinion considers the waw as a simple conjunction with 'amma' omitted and the fa' indicating it. Al-Sakkaki's usage in al-Miftah combining both is noted. Finally, the vocalization 'ba'du' with dammah is explained as it is an adverb functioning as a predicate in a deleted sentence.

Key Terms
أَمَّا بَعْدُ
مَهْمَا يَكُنْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ بَعْدُ
العِوَض

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'amma ba'd' linguistically originates from a conditional sentence, and the variant 'wa ba'd' involves a debated substitution of the waw for 'amma' or its role as a conjunction.
